For other uses, see <a href="/wiki/Serbia_(disambiguation)" class="mw-disambig" title="Serbia (disambiguation)">Serbia (disambiguation)</a> and <a href="/wiki/Serb_Republic_(disambiguation)" class="mw-redirect mw-disambig" title="Serb Republic (disambiguation)">Serb Republic (disambiguation)</a>.</div>

<ol style="list-style-type: lower-alpha; margin-left: 1em; font-size:90%;">
<li value="1">From the <a href="/wiki/Serbian_Despotate" title="Serbian Despotate">fall of Smederevo</a> until conquest of <a href="/wiki/Belgrade" title="Belgrade">Belgrade</a>, <a href="/wiki/Macva" class="mw-redirect" title="Macva">Mačva</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vojvodina" title="Vojvodina">Vojvodina</a></li>
</ol>
</div>

<p><b>Serbia</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'s' in 'sigh'">s</span><span title="/ɜːr/: 'ur' in 'fur'">ɜːr</span><span title="'b' in 'buy'">b</span><span title="/iː/ or /ɪ/: 'y' in 'happy'">i</span><span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">ə</span></span>/</a></span><small class="nowrap metadata">&#160;(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap"><a href="/wiki/File:En-us-Serbia.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20" /></a>&#160;</span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/5/50/En-us-Serbia.ogg" class="internal" title="En-us-Serbia.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</small></span>, <a href="/wiki/Serbian_language" title="Serbian language">Serbian</a>: <span lang="sr">Србија / <i>Srbija</i></span>, <small>IPA:&#160;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Serbo-Croatian" title="Help:IPA/Serbo-Croatian">[sř̩bija]</a></span>), officially the <b>Republic of Serbia</b> (<a href="/wiki/Serbian_language" title="Serbian language">Serbian</a>: <span lang="sr">Република Србија / <i>Republika Srbija</i></span>), is a <a href="/wiki/Landlocked_country" title="Landlocked country">landlocked</a> country situated at the crossroads of <a href="/wiki/Central_Europe" title="Central Europe">Central</a><sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Europe" title="Southeast Europe">Southeast Europe</a> in the southern <a href="/wiki/Pannonian_Plain" class="mw-redirect" title="Pannonian Plain">Pannonian Plain</a> and the central <a href="/wiki/Balkans" title="Balkans">Balkans</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Lidia_Razowska-Jaworek.2C_CRC_Press_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lidia_Razowska-Jaworek.2C_CRC_Press-7">[7]</a></sup> It borders <a href="/wiki/Hungary" title="Hungary">Hungary</a> to the north; <a href="/wiki/Romania" title="Romania">Romania</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bulgaria" title="Bulgaria">Bulgaria</a> to the east; <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Macedonia" title="Republic of Macedonia">Macedonia</a> to the south; <a href="/wiki/Croatia" title="Croatia">Croatia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Bosnia and Herzegovina">Bosnia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Montenegro" title="Montenegro">Montenegro</a> to the west and claims a border with <a href="/wiki/Albania" title="Albania">Albania</a> through the <a href="/wiki/Political_status_of_Kosovo" title="Political status of Kosovo">disputed</a> territory of <a href="/wiki/Kosovo" title="Kosovo">Kosovo</a>. Serbia numbers around 7 million residents;<sup id="cite_ref-auto_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-8">[8]</a></sup> its capital, <a href="/wiki/Belgrade" title="Belgrade">Belgrade</a>, ranks among the oldest<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Lidia_Razowska-Jaworek.2C_CRC_Press_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lidia_Razowska-Jaworek.2C_CRC_Press-7">[7]</a></sup> and largest cities in <a href="/wiki/Southeastern_Europe" class="mw-redirect" title="Southeastern Europe">Southeastern Europe</a>.</p>
<p>Following the <a href="/wiki/Slavic_migrations" class="mw-redirect" title="Slavic migrations">Slavic migrations</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Balkans" title="Balkans">Balkans</a> postdating the 6th century, <a href="/wiki/Serbs" title="Serbs">Serbs</a> established several <a href="/wiki/Principality_of_Serbia_(medieval)" title="Principality of Serbia (medieval)">states</a> in the early Middle Ages. The <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Serbia_(medieval)" title="Kingdom of Serbia (medieval)">Serbian Kingdom</a> obtained recognition by <a href="/wiki/Rome" title="Rome">Rome</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" title="Byzantine Empire">Byzantine Empire</a> in 1217, reaching its peak in 1346 as a relatively short-lived <a href="/wiki/Serbian_Empire" title="Serbian Empire">Serbian Empire</a>. By the mid-16th century, the entire modern-day Serbia was annexed by the <a href="/wiki/Ottomans" class="mw-redirect" title="Ottomans">Ottomans</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ottoman%E2%80%93Habsburg_wars" title="Ottoman–Habsburg wars">at times interrupted</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Habsburg_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Habsburg Empire">Habsburg Empire</a>, which <a href="/wiki/Ottoman%E2%80%93Habsburg_wars" title="Ottoman–Habsburg wars">started expanding</a> towards <a href="/wiki/Central_Serbia" title="Central Serbia">Central Serbia</a> from the end of the 17th century, while maintaining a foothold in modern-day <a href="/wiki/Vojvodina" title="Vojvodina">Vojvodina</a>. In the early 19th century, the <a href="/wiki/Serbian_Revolution" title="Serbian Revolution">Serbian Revolution</a> established the <a href="/wiki/Principality_of_Serbia" title="Principality of Serbia">nation-state</a> as the region's first <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_monarchy" title="Constitutional monarchy">constitutional monarchy</a>, which subsequently expanded its territory.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> Following disastrous casualties in <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>, and the subsequent unification of the <a href="/wiki/Voivodeship_of_Serbia_and_Banat_of_Temeschwar" title="Voivodeship of Serbia and Banat of Temeschwar">former Habsburg crownland of Vojvodina</a> (and other territories) with <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Serbia" title="Kingdom of Serbia">Serbia</a>, the country co-founded <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Serbs,_Croats_and_Slovenes" class="mw-redirect" title="Kingdom of Serbs, Croats and Slovenes">Yugoslavia</a> with other South Slavic peoples, which would exist in various political formations until the <a href="/wiki/Yugoslav_Wars" title="Yugoslav Wars">Yugoslav Wars</a> of the 1990s. During the <a href="/wiki/Breakup_of_Yugoslavia" title="Breakup of Yugoslavia">breakup of Yugoslavia</a>, Serbia formed a <a href="/wiki/Serbia_and_Montenegro" title="Serbia and Montenegro">union with Montenegro</a> which dissolved peacefully in 2006, when Serbia reestablished its independence. In 2008, the parliament of the province of <a href="/wiki/Kosovo" title="Kosovo">Kosovo</a> unilaterally declared independence, with mixed responses from the international community.</p>
<p>Serbia is a member of numerous organizations such as the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">UN</a>, <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Europe" title="Council of Europe">CoE</a>, <a href="/wiki/Organization_for_Security_and_Co-operation_in_Europe" title="Organization for Security and Co-operation in Europe">OSCE</a>, <a href="/wiki/Partnership_for_Peace" title="Partnership for Peace">PfP</a>, <a href="/wiki/Organization_of_the_Black_Sea_Economic_Cooperation" title="Organization of the Black Sea Economic Cooperation">BSEC</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Central_European_Free_Trade_Agreement" title="Central European Free Trade Agreement">CEFTA</a>. An <a href="/wiki/Accession_of_Serbia_to_the_European_Union" title="Accession of Serbia to the European Union">EU membership candidate</a> since 2012,<sup id="cite_ref-bbc_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc-11">[11]</a></sup> Serbia has been negotiating <a href="/wiki/Accession_of_Serbia_to_the_European_Union" title="Accession of Serbia to the European Union">its EU accession</a> since January 2014. The country is acceding to the <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Organization" title="World Trade Organization">WTO</a><sup id="cite_ref-WTO_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WTO-12">[12]</a></sup> and is a militarily <a href="/wiki/Neutrality_(international_relations)" class="mw-redirect" title="Neutrality (international relations)">neutral</a> state. Serbia is an upper-middle income economy<sup id="cite_ref-Serbia:_On_the_Way_to_EU_Accession_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Serbia:_On_the_Way_to_EU_Accession-13">[13]</a></sup> with a dominant service sector, followed by the industrial sector and agriculture. The country ranks high by the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_Human_Development_Index" title="List of countries by Human Development Index">Human Development Index</a> (66th),<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_Social_Progress_Index" title="List of countries by Social Progress Index">Social Progress Index</a> (45th)<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> as well as the <a href="/wiki/Global_Peace_Index" title="Global Peace Index">Global Peace Index</a> (56th).<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-39"><a href="#Public_holidays"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">Public holidays</span></a></li>
<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-40"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>
<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-41"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">11</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>
<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-42"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">12</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>
</ul>
</div>
<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Names_of_the_Serbs_and_Serbia" title="Names of the Serbs and Serbia">Names of the Serbs and Serbia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Origin_hypotheses_of_the_Serbs" title="Origin hypotheses of the Serbs">Origin hypotheses of the Serbs</a></div>
<p>The origin of the name, <i>"Serbia"</i> is unclear. Various authors mentioned names of <a href="/wiki/Serbs" title="Serbs">Serbs</a> (<a href="/wiki/Serbian_language" title="Serbian language">Serbian</a>: <span lang="sr">Srbi</span> / Срби) and <a href="/wiki/Sorbs" title="Sorbs">Sorbs</a> (<a href="/wiki/Upper_Sorbian_language" title="Upper Sorbian language">Upper Sorbian</a>: <i>Serbja</i>; <a href="/wiki/Lower_Sorbian_language" title="Lower Sorbian language">Lower Sorbian</a>: <i>Serby</i>) in different variants: Surbii, Suurbi, Serbloi, Zeriuani, Sorabi, Surben, Sarbi, Serbii, Serboi, Zirbi, Surbi, Sorben,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPetkovi.C4.8719269_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPetkovi.C4.8719269-17">[17]</a></sup> etc. These authors used these names to refer to Serbs and Sorbs in areas where their historical (or current) presence was/is not disputed (notably in the <a href="/wiki/Balkans" title="Balkans">Balkans</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lusatia" title="Lusatia">Lusatia</a>), but there are also sources that mention same or similar names in other parts of the World (most notably in the Asiatic <a href="/wiki/Sarmatia" class="mw-redirect" title="Sarmatia">Sarmatia</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Caucasus" title="Caucasus">Caucasus</a>).</p>
<p>Theoretically, the root *sъrbъ has been variously connected with Russian <i>paserb</i> (пасерб, "stepson"), Ukrainian <i>priserbitisya</i> (присербитися, "join in"), Old <a href="/wiki/Indo-Aryan_languages" title="Indo-Aryan languages">Indic</a> <i>sarbh-</i> ("fight, cut, kill"), Latin <i>sero</i> ("make up, constitute"), and Greek <i>siro</i> (ειρω, "repeat").<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> However, Polish linguist <a href="/wiki/Stanis%C5%82aw_Rospond" title="Stanisław Rospond">Stanisław Rospond</a> (1906–1982) derived the denomination of <i>Srb</i> from <i>srbati</i> (<a href="/wiki/Cf." title="Cf.">cf.</a> <i>sorbo</i>, <i>absorbo</i>).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELukaszewicz1998132_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELukaszewicz1998132-19">[19]</a></sup> Sorbian scholar H. Schuster-Šewc suggested a connection with the Proto-Slavic verb for "to slurp" *sьrb-, with cognates such as <i>сербать</i> (Russian, Ukrainian), <i>сербаць</i> (Belarusian), <i>srbati</i> (Slovak), <i>сърбам</i>(Bulgarian) and <i>серебати</i> (Old Russian).<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup></p>
<p>From 1945 to 1963, the official name for Serbia was the <i>People's Republic of Serbia</i>, which became the <i><a href="/wiki/Socialist_Republic_of_Serbia" title="Socialist Republic of Serbia">Socialist Republic of Serbia</a></i> from 1963 to 1990. Since 1990, the official name of the country is the <i>"Republic of Serbia"</i>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Serbia" title="History of Serbia">History of Serbia</a></div>
<div class="thumb tmulti tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:248px;max-width:248px">
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:132px;max-width:132px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Lepenski_Vir_Head.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Lepenski_Vir_Head.JPG/130px-Lepenski_Vir_Head.JPG" width="130" height="173" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Lepenski_Vir_Head.JPG/195px-Lepenski_Vir_Head.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Lepenski_Vir_Head.JPG/260px-Lepenski_Vir_Head.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1536" data-file-height="2048" /></a></div>
</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:112px;max-width:112px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Vinca_clay_figure_02.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Vinca_clay_figure_02.jpg/110px-Vinca_clay_figure_02.jpg" width="110" height="177" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Vinca_clay_figure_02.jpg/165px-Vinca_clay_figure_02.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Vinca_clay_figure_02.jpg/220px-Vinca_clay_figure_02.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2237" data-file-height="3593" /></a></div>
</div>

</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Prehistory">Prehistory</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Prehistoric_sites_in_Serbia" title="Prehistoric sites in Serbia">Prehistoric sites in Serbia</a></div>
<p>Archeological evidence of <a href="/wiki/Paleolithic" title="Paleolithic">Paleolithic</a> settlements on the territory of present-day Serbia are scarce. A fragment of a human jaw, was found in <a href="/wiki/Si%C4%87evo" class="mw-redirect" title="Sićevo">Sićevo</a> (Mala Balanica) and believed to be up to 525,000—397,000 years old.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup></p>
<p>Approximately around 6,500 years BC, during the <a href="/wiki/Neolithic" title="Neolithic">Neolithic</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Star%C4%8Devo_culture" title="Starčevo culture">Starčevo</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Vin%C4%8Da_culture" title="Vinča culture">Vinča</a> cultures existed in or near modern-day Belgrade and dominated much of the <a href="/wiki/Southeastern_Europe" class="mw-redirect" title="Southeastern Europe">Southeastern Europe</a>, (as well as parts of <a href="/wiki/Central_Europe" title="Central Europe">Central Europe</a> and <a href="/wiki/Asia_Minor" class="mw-redirect" title="Asia Minor">Asia Minor</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-Vinca_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Vinca-22">[22]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ancient_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ancient-23">[23]</a></sup> Two important local archeological sites from this era, <a href="/wiki/Lepenski_Vir" title="Lepenski Vir">Lepenski Vir</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vin%C4%8Da-Belo_Brdo" title="Vinča-Belo Brdo">Vinča-Belo Brdo</a>, still exist near the banks of the <a href="/wiki/Danube" title="Danube">Danube</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ancient_history">Ancient history</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Roman_heritage_in_Serbia" title="Roman heritage in Serbia">Roman heritage in Serbia</a></div>
<p>During the <a href="/wiki/Iron_Age" title="Iron Age">Iron Age</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thracians" title="Thracians">Thracians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dacians" title="Dacians">Dacians</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Illyrians" title="Illyrians">Illyrians</a> were encountered by the <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greeks" class="mw-redirect" title="Ancient Greeks">Ancient Greeks</a> during their expansion into the south of modern Serbia in the 4th century BC; the northwesternmost point of <a href="/wiki/Alexander_the_Great" title="Alexander the Great">Alexander the Great</a>'s empire being the town of <a href="/wiki/Kale-Kr%C5%A1evica" title="Kale-Krševica">Kale-Krševica</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:NOTRS" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:NOTRS"><span title="This claim needs references to better sources. (March 2017)">better&#160;source&#160;needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The Celtic tribe of <a href="/wiki/Scordisci" title="Scordisci">Scordisci</a> settled throughout the area in the 3rd century BC and formed a tribal state, building several fortifications, including their capital at <a href="/wiki/Singidunum" title="Singidunum">Singidunum</a> (present-day Belgrade) and Naissos (present-day <a href="/wiki/Ni%C5%A1" title="Niš">Niš</a>).</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Romuliana.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Romuliana.jpg/250px-Romuliana.jpg" width="250" height="106" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Romuliana.jpg/375px-Romuliana.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Romuliana.jpg/500px-Romuliana.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="338" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Romuliana.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Remnants of <a href="/wiki/Gamzigrad" title="Gamzigrad">Felix Romuliana Imperial Palace</a>, <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">UNESCO World Heritage Site</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Rome" title="Ancient Rome">Romans</a> conquered much of the territory in the 2nd century BC. In 167 BC the <a href="/wiki/Roman_province" title="Roman province">Roman province</a> of <a href="/wiki/Illyricum_(Roman_province)" title="Illyricum (Roman province)">Illyricum</a> was established; the remainder was conquered around 75 BC, forming the Roman province of <a href="/wiki/Moesia_Superior" class="mw-redirect" title="Moesia Superior">Moesia Superior</a>; the modern-day <a href="/wiki/Srem_District" title="Srem District">Srem</a> region was conquered in 9 BC; and Bačka and Banat in 106 AD after the <a href="/wiki/Trajan%27s_Dacian_Wars" title="Trajan's Dacian Wars">Dacian Wars</a>. As a result of this, contemporary Serbia extends fully or partially over several former Roman provinces, including <a href="/wiki/Moesia" title="Moesia">Moesia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pannonia" title="Pannonia">Pannonia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Praevalitana" title="Praevalitana">Praevalitana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dalmatia" title="Dalmatia">Dalmatia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dacia" title="Dacia">Dacia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Macedonia_(region)" title="Macedonia (region)">Macedonia</a>.</p>
<p>The chief towns of <a href="/wiki/Upper_Moesia" class="mw-redirect" title="Upper Moesia">Upper Moesia</a> (and wider) were: Singidunum (Belgrade), <a href="/wiki/Viminacium" title="Viminacium">Viminacium</a> (now <a href="/wiki/Kostolac" title="Kostolac">Old Kostolac</a>), <a href="/wiki/Remesiana" title="Remesiana">Remesiana</a> (now <a href="/wiki/Bela_Palanka" title="Bela Palanka">Bela Palanka</a>), Naissos (Niš), and <a href="/wiki/Sirmium" title="Sirmium">Sirmium</a> (now <a href="/wiki/Sremska_Mitrovica" title="Sremska Mitrovica">Sremska Mitrovica</a>), the latter of which served as a Roman capital during the <a href="/wiki/Tetrarchy" title="Tetrarchy">Tetrarchy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> Seventeen Roman Emperors were born in the area of modern-day Serbia, second only to contemporary Italy.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> The most famous of these was <a href="/wiki/Constantine_the_Great" title="Constantine the Great">Constantine the Great</a>, the first Christian Emperor, who issued an edict ordering <a href="/wiki/Edict_of_Milan" title="Edict of Milan">religious tolerance throughout the Empire</a>.</p>
<p>When the Roman Empire was divided in 395, most of Serbia remained under the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Roman_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Eastern Roman Empire">Eastern Roman Empire</a>, while its northwestern parts were included in the <a href="/wiki/Western_Roman_Empire" title="Western Roman Empire">Western Roman Empire</a>. By the early 6th century, <a href="/wiki/South_Slavs" title="South Slavs">South Slavs</a> were present throughout the Byzantine Empire in large numbers.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Middle_Ages">Middle Ages</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Serbia_in_the_Middle_Ages" title="Serbia in the Middle Ages">Serbia in the Middle Ages</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:272px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Detail_of_Krunisanje_Cara_Du%C5%A1ana_by_Paja_Jovanovi%C4%87.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/1d/Detail_of_Krunisanje_Cara_Du%C5%A1ana_by_Paja_Jovanovi%C4%87.jpg/270px-Detail_of_Krunisanje_Cara_Du%C5%A1ana_by_Paja_Jovanovi%C4%87.jpg" width="270" height="180" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/1d/Detail_of_Krunisanje_Cara_Du%C5%A1ana_by_Paja_Jovanovi%C4%87.jpg/405px-Detail_of_Krunisanje_Cara_Du%C5%A1ana_by_Paja_Jovanovi%C4%87.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/1d/Detail_of_Krunisanje_Cara_Du%C5%A1ana_by_Paja_Jovanovi%C4%87.jpg/540px-Detail_of_Krunisanje_Cara_Du%C5%A1ana_by_Paja_Jovanovi%C4%87.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="683" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Detail_of_Krunisanje_Cara_Du%C5%A1ana_by_Paja_Jovanovi%C4%87.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<i><a href="/wiki/The_Proclamation_of_Du%C5%A1an%27s_Law_Codex" title="The Proclamation of Dušan's Law Codex">The Proclamation of Dušan's Law Codex</a></i> in <a href="/wiki/Skopje_Fortress" title="Skopje Fortress">Skopje Fortress</a> in 1349</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Serbs, a Slavic tribe that settled the Balkans in the 6th or early 7th century, established the <a href="/wiki/Principality_of_Serbia_(medieval)" title="Principality of Serbia (medieval)">Serbian Principality</a> by the 8th century. It was said in 822 that the Serbs inhabited the greater part of Roman Dalmatia, their territory spanning what is today southwestern Serbia and parts of neighbouring countries. Meanwhile, the Byzantine Empire and Bulgarian Empire held other parts of the territory. Christianity was adopted by the Serbian rulers in ca. 870, and by the mid-10th-century the Serbian state stretched the <a href="/wiki/Adriatic_Sea" title="Adriatic Sea">Adriatic Sea</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Neretva" title="Neretva">Neretva</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Sava" title="Sava">Sava</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Pomoravlje_(region)" class="mw-redirect" title="Pomoravlje (region)">Morava</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Lake_Skadar" title="Lake Skadar">Skadar</a>. Between 1166 and 1371 Serbia was ruled by the <a href="/wiki/Nemanji%C4%87_dynasty" title="Nemanjić dynasty">Nemanjić dynasty</a> (which legacy is especially cherished), under whom the state was elevated to <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Serbia_(medieval)" title="Kingdom of Serbia (medieval)">a kingdom</a> (and briefly <a href="/wiki/Serbian_Empire" title="Serbian Empire">an empire</a>) and Serbian bishopric to <a href="/wiki/Serbian_Orthodox_Church" title="Serbian Orthodox Church">an autocephalous archbishopric</a> (through the effort of <a href="/wiki/Saint_Sava" title="Saint Sava">Sava</a>, the country's patron saint). Monuments of the Nemanjić period survives in many <a href="/wiki/Serbian_Orthodox_monasteries" class="mw-redirect" title="Serbian Orthodox monasteries">monasteries</a> (several being <a href="/wiki/List_of_World_Heritage_Sites_in_Serbia" title="List of World Heritage Sites in Serbia">World Heritage</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Forts_in_Serbia" class="mw-redirect" title="Forts in Serbia">fortifications</a>. During these centuries the Serbian state (and influence) expanded significantly. The northern part, <a href="/wiki/Vojvodina" title="Vojvodina">Vojvodina</a>, was ruled by the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Hungary" title="Kingdom of Hungary">Kingdom of Hungary</a>. The period known as the <a href="/wiki/Fall_of_the_Serbian_Empire" title="Fall of the Serbian Empire">Fall of the Serbian Empire</a> saw the once-powerful state fragmented into duchies, culminating in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Kosovo" title="Battle of Kosovo">Battle of Kosovo</a> (1389) against the rising <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Serbian_Despotate" title="Serbian Despotate">Serbian Despotate</a> was finally conquered by the Ottomans in 1459. The Ottoman threat and eventual conquest saw large migrations of Serbs to the west and north.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTE.C4.86orovi.C4.872001ch._I_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTE.C4.86orovi.C4.872001ch._I-28">[28]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ottoman_and_Habsburg_rule">Ottoman and Habsburg rule</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Serbia" title="Ottoman Serbia">Ottoman Serbia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Serbia_(1718%E2%80%9339)" title="Kingdom of Serbia (1718–39)">Kingdom of Serbia (1718–39)</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Great_Migrations_of_the_Serbs" title="Great Migrations of the Serbs">Great Migrations of the Serbs</a></div>
<p>After the loss of independence to the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Hungary" title="Kingdom of Hungary">Kingdom of Hungary</a> and the Ottoman Empire, Serbia briefly regained sovereignty under <a href="/wiki/Jovan_Nenad" title="Jovan Nenad">Jovan Nenad</a> in the 16th century. Three Habsburg invasions and numerous rebellions constantly challenged Ottoman rule. One famous incident was the <a href="/wiki/Banat_Uprising" class="mw-redirect" title="Banat Uprising">Banat Uprising</a> in 1595, which was part of the <a href="/wiki/Long_War_(Ottoman_wars)" class="mw-redirect" title="Long War (Ottoman wars)">Long War</a> between the Ottomans and the <a href="/wiki/Habsburgs" class="mw-redirect" title="Habsburgs">Habsburgs</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> The area of modern Vojvodina endured a century-long Ottoman occupation before being ceded to the <a href="/wiki/Habsburg_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Habsburg Empire">Habsburg Empire</a> at the end of the 17th century under the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Karlowitz" title="Treaty of Karlowitz">Treaty of Karlowitz</a>.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:272px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Serbmigra.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/48/Serbmigra.jpg/270px-Serbmigra.jpg" width="270" height="181" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/48/Serbmigra.jpg/405px-Serbmigra.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/48/Serbmigra.jpg/540px-Serbmigra.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1070" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Serbmigra.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Great_Migrations_of_the_Serbs" title="Great Migrations of the Serbs">Great Migrations into Habsburg Empire</a>, led by Patriarch <a href="/wiki/Arsenije_III_%C4%8Carnojevi%C4%87" title="Arsenije III Čarnojević">Arsenije III Čarnojević</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In all Serb lands south of the rivers Danube and Sava, the nobility was eliminated and the peasantry was <a href="/wiki/Serfdom" title="Serfdom">enserfed</a> to Ottoman masters, while much of the clergy fled or were confined to the isolated monasteries. Under the Ottoman system, Serbs, as Christians, were considered an <a href="/wiki/Rayah" title="Rayah">inferior class</a> of people and subjected to heavy taxes, and a small portion of the Serbian populace experienced <a href="/wiki/Islamisation" class="mw-redirect" title="Islamisation">Islamisation</a>. The Ottomans abolished the <a href="/wiki/Serbian_Patriarchate_of_Pe%C4%87" title="Serbian Patriarchate of Peć">Serbian Patriarchate of Peć</a> (1463), but reestablished it in 1557, providing for limited continuation of Serbian cultural traditions within the empire.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup></p>
<p>As the <a href="/wiki/Great_Serb_Migrations" class="mw-redirect" title="Great Serb Migrations">Great Serb Migrations</a> depopulated most of southern Serbia, the Serbs sought refuge across the Danube River in <a href="/wiki/Vojvodina" title="Vojvodina">Vojvodina</a> to the north and the <a href="/wiki/Military_Frontier" title="Military Frontier">Military Frontier</a> in the west, where they were granted rights by the Austrian crown under measures such as the <i>Statuta Wallachorum</i> of 1630. The ecclesiastical center of the Serbs also moved northwards, to the Metropolitanate of <a href="/wiki/Sremski_Karlovci" title="Sremski Karlovci">Sremski Karlovci</a>, as the <a href="/wiki/Serbian_Patriarchate_of_Pe%C4%87" title="Serbian Patriarchate of Peć">Serbian Patriarchate of Peć</a> was once-again abolished by the Ottomans in 1766.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> Following several petitions, the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Holy Roman Emperor">Holy Roman Emperor</a> <a href="/wiki/Leopold_I,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Leopold I, Holy Roman Emperor">Leopold I</a> formally granted Serbs who wished to leave the right to their autonomous crownland.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1718–39, the <a href="/wiki/Habsburg_Monarchy" title="Habsburg Monarchy">Habsburg Monarchy</a> occupied <a href="/wiki/Central_Serbia" title="Central Serbia">Central Serbia</a> and established the "<a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Serbia_(1718%E2%80%9339)" title="Kingdom of Serbia (1718–39)">Kingdom of Serbia</a>". Apart from Vojvodina and <a href="/wiki/Zemun" title="Zemun">Northern Belgrade</a> which were absorbed into the Habsburg Empire, Central Serbia was occupied by the Habsburgs again in <a href="/wiki/Habsburg-occupied_Serbia_(1686%E2%80%9391)" title="Habsburg-occupied Serbia (1686–91)">1686–91</a> and <a href="/wiki/Habsburg-occupied_Serbia_(1788%E2%80%9392)" title="Habsburg-occupied Serbia (1788–92)">in 1788–92</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Revolution_and_independence">Revolution and independence</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Serbian_Revolution" title="Serbian Revolution">Serbian Revolution</a>, <a href="/wiki/Principality_of_Serbia" title="Principality of Serbia">Principality of Serbia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Serbia" title="Kingdom of Serbia">Kingdom of Serbia</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Serbian_Vojvodina" title="Serbian Vojvodina">Serbian Vojvodina</a> and <a href="/wiki/May_Overthrow" class="mw-redirect" title="May Overthrow">May Overthrow</a></div>
<div class="thumb tmulti tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:293px;max-width:293px">
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:152px;max-width:152px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Dositej_Obradovic.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Dositej_Obradovic.jpg/150px-Dositej_Obradovic.jpg" width="150" height="193" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Dositej_Obradovic.jpg/225px-Dositej_Obradovic.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Dositej_Obradovic.jpg/300px-Dositej_Obradovic.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2731" data-file-height="3517" /></a></div>
</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:137px;max-width:137px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:MilosObrenovic_1848.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/MilosObrenovic_1848.jpg/135px-MilosObrenovic_1848.jpg" width="135" height="191" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/MilosObrenovic_1848.jpg/203px-MilosObrenovic_1848.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/MilosObrenovic_1848.jpg/270px-MilosObrenovic_1848.jpg 2x" data-file-width="495" data-file-height="702" /></a></div>
</div>
<div style="clear:left"></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:left;background-color:transparent"><b>Left:</b> <a href="/wiki/Dositej_Obradovi%C4%87" title="Dositej Obradović">Dositej Obradović</a>, an influential protagonist of the Serbian national and cultural renaissance, he advocated <a href="/wiki/Age_of_Enlightenment" title="Age of Enlightenment">Enlightenment</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rationalism" title="Rationalism">rationalist</a> ideas<br />
<b>Right:</b> <a href="/wiki/Milo%C5%A1_Obrenovi%C4%87" title="Miloš Obrenović">Miloš Obrenović</a> leader of the <a href="/wiki/Second_Serbian_Uprising" title="Second Serbian Uprising">Second Serbian Uprising</a> in <a href="/wiki/Takovo" title="Takovo">Takovo</a>, the second phase of the <a href="/wiki/Serbian_Revolution" title="Serbian Revolution">Serbian Revolution</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Serbian_Revolution" title="Serbian Revolution">Serbian Revolution</a> for independence from the Ottoman Empire lasted eleven years, from 1804 until 1815.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> The revolution comprised two separate uprisings which gained autonomy from the Ottoman Empire that eventually evolved towards full independence (1835–1867).<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-nytimes_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nytimes-36">[36]</a></sup> During the <a href="/wiki/First_Serbian_Uprising" title="First Serbian Uprising">First Serbian Uprising</a>, led by Duke <a href="/wiki/Kara%C4%91or%C4%91e_Petrovi%C4%87" class="mw-redirect" title="Karađorđe Petrović">Karađorđe Petrović</a>, Serbia was independent for almost a decade before the Ottoman army was able to reoccupy the country. Shortly after this, the <a href="/wiki/Second_Serbian_Uprising" title="Second Serbian Uprising">Second Serbian Uprising</a> began. Led by <a href="/wiki/Milo%C5%A1_Obrenovi%C4%87" title="Miloš Obrenović">Miloš Obrenović</a>, it ended in 1815 with a compromise between Serbian revolutionaries and Ottoman authorities.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> Likewise, Serbia was one of the first nations in the Balkans to abolish <a href="/wiki/Feudalism" title="Feudalism">feudalism</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> The Convention of Ackerman in 1826, the Treaty of Adrianople in 1829 and finally, the <a href="/wiki/Hatt-i_Sharif" class="mw-redirect" title="Hatt-i Sharif">Hatt-i Sharif</a>, recognized the <a href="/wiki/Suzerainty" title="Suzerainty">suzerainty</a> of Serbia. The first Serbian Constitution was adopted on 15 February 1835.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup></p>
<p>Following the clashes between the Ottoman army and Serbs in Belgrade in 1862, and under pressure from the <a href="/wiki/Great_Powers" class="mw-redirect" title="Great Powers">Great Powers</a>, by 1867 the last Turkish soldiers left the Principality, making the country <i>de facto</i> independent. By enacting a new constitution without consulting the Porte, <a href="/wiki/Jovan_Ristic" class="mw-redirect" title="Jovan Ristic">Serbian diplomats</a> confirmed the <i>de facto</i> independence of the country. In 1876, Serbia declared war on the Ottoman Empire, proclaiming its unification with <a href="/wiki/Bosnia_(region)" title="Bosnia (region)">Bosnia</a>.</p>
<p>The formal independence of the country was internationally recognized at the <a href="/wiki/Congress_of_Berlin" title="Congress of Berlin">Congress of Berlin</a> in 1878, which formally ended the <a href="/wiki/Russo-Turkish_War_(1877%E2%80%931878)" title="Russo-Turkish War (1877–1878)">Russo-Turkish War</a>; this treaty, however, prohibited Serbia from uniting with Bosnia by placing Bosnia under <a href="/wiki/Austria-Hungary" title="Austria-Hungary">Austro-Hungarian</a> occupation, alongside the occupation of <a href="/wiki/Sanjak_of_Novi_Pazar" title="Sanjak of Novi Pazar">Sanjak of Novi Pazar</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> From 1815 to 1903, the Principality of Serbia was ruled by the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Obrenovi%C4%87" class="mw-redirect" title="House of Obrenović">House of Obrenović</a>, save for the rule of Prince <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Kara%C4%91or%C4%91evi%C4%87,_Prince_of_Serbia" title="Alexander Karađorđević, Prince of Serbia">Aleksandar Karađorđević</a> between 1842 and 1858. In 1882, Serbia became a <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Serbia" title="Kingdom of Serbia">Kingdom</a>, ruled by <a href="/wiki/Milan_I_of_Serbia" title="Milan I of Serbia">King Milan I</a>. The <a href="/wiki/House_of_Kara%C4%91or%C4%91evi%C4%87" class="mw-redirect" title="House of Karađorđević">House of Karađorđević</a>, descendants of the revolutionary leader Karađorđe Petrović, assumed power in 1903 following the <a href="/wiki/May_Overthrow" class="mw-redirect" title="May Overthrow">May Overthrow</a>. In the north, the <a href="/wiki/Revolutions_of_1848_in_the_Habsburg_areas" class="mw-redirect" title="Revolutions of 1848 in the Habsburg areas">1848 revolution in Austria</a> led to the establishment of the autonomous territory of <a href="/wiki/Serbian_Vojvodina" title="Serbian Vojvodina">Serbian Vojvodina</a>; by 1849, the region was transformed into the <a href="/wiki/Voivodeship_of_Serbia_and_Banat_of_Temeschwar" title="Voivodeship of Serbia and Banat of Temeschwar">Voivodeship of Serbia and Banat of Temeschwar</a>.</p>
<h3><span id="Balkan_Wars,_World_War_I_and_the_First_Yugoslavia"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Balkan_Wars.2C_World_War_I_and_the_First_Yugoslavia">Balkan Wars, World War I and the First Yugoslavia</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Balkan_Wars" title="Balkan Wars">Balkan Wars</a>, <a href="/wiki/Serbian_Campaign_of_World_War_I" title="Serbian Campaign of World War I">Serbian Campaign of World War I</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Yugoslavia" title="Kingdom of Yugoslavia">Kingdom of Yugoslavia</a></div>
<p>In the course of the <a href="/wiki/First_Balkan_War" title="First Balkan War">First Balkan War</a> in 1912, the <a href="/wiki/Balkan_League" title="Balkan League">Balkan League</a> defeated the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a> and captured its <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_London,_1913" class="mw-redirect" title="Treaty of London, 1913">European territories</a>, which enabled territorial expansion into <a href="/wiki/Ra%C5%A1ka_(region)" title="Raška (region)">Raška</a> and Kosovo. The <a href="/wiki/Second_Balkan_War" title="Second Balkan War">Second Balkan War</a> soon ensued when Bulgaria turned on its former allies, but was defeated, resulting in the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Bucharest_(1913)" title="Treaty of Bucharest (1913)">Treaty of Bucharest</a>. In two years, Serbia enlarged its territory by 80% and its population by 50%;<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> it also suffered high casualties on the eve of World War I, with around 20,000 dead.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> Austria-Hungary became wary of the rising regional power on its borders and its potential to become an anchor for unification of all South Slavs, and the relationship between the two countries became tense.</p>
<div class="thumb tmulti tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:313px;max-width:313px">
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:147px;max-width:147px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:NikolaPasic--serbiaherpeopleh00petruoft.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/NikolaPasic--serbiaherpeopleh00petruoft.png/145px-NikolaPasic--serbiaherpeopleh00petruoft.png" width="145" height="211" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/NikolaPasic--serbiaherpeopleh00petruoft.png/218px-NikolaPasic--serbiaherpeopleh00petruoft.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/NikolaPasic--serbiaherpeopleh00petruoft.png/290px-NikolaPasic--serbiaherpeopleh00petruoft.png 2x" data-file-width="591" data-file-height="858" /></a></div>
</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:162px;max-width:162px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Mihajlo_Pupin.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Mihajlo_Pupin.jpg/160px-Mihajlo_Pupin.jpg" width="160" height="210" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Mihajlo_Pupin.jpg/240px-Mihajlo_Pupin.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Mihajlo_Pupin.jpg/320px-Mihajlo_Pupin.jpg 2x" data-file-width="323" data-file-height="424" /></a></div>
</div>
<div style="clear:left"></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:left;background-color:transparent"><b>Left:</b> <a href="/wiki/Nikola_Pa%C5%A1i%C4%87" title="Nikola Pašić">Nikola Pašić</a>, Prime Minister during World War I<br />
<b>Right:</b> <a href="/wiki/Mihajlo_Pupin" title="Mihajlo Pupin">Mihajlo Pupin</a>, scientist, influenced the final decisions of the <a href="/wiki/Paris_Peace_Conference,_1919" title="Paris Peace Conference, 1919">Paris Peace Conference</a> when the borders of the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Yugoslavia" title="Kingdom of Yugoslavia">Kingdom</a> were drawn</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Assassination_in_Sarajevo" class="mw-redirect" title="Assassination in Sarajevo">assassination</a> of <a href="/wiki/Archduke_Franz_Ferdinand_of_Austria" title="Archduke Franz Ferdinand of Austria">Archduke Franz Ferdinand of Austria</a> on 28 June 1914 in <a href="/wiki/Sarajevo" title="Sarajevo">Sarajevo</a> by <a href="/wiki/Gavrilo_Princip" title="Gavrilo Princip">Gavrilo Princip</a>, a member of the <a href="/wiki/Young_Bosnia" title="Young Bosnia">Young Bosnia</a> organization, led to Austria-Hungary declaring war on Serbia.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> In defense of Serbia, and to maintain her status as a Great Power, <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russia</a> mobilized its troops, which resulted in Austria-Hungary's ally <a href="/wiki/German_Empire" title="German Empire">Germany</a> declaring war on Russia.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> Serbia won the first major battles of World War I, including the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Cer" title="Battle of Cer">Battle of Cer</a> and <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Kolubara" title="Battle of Kolubara">Battle of Kolubara</a> – marking the first <a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_I" title="Allies of World War I">Allied</a> victories against the <a href="/wiki/Central_Powers" title="Central Powers">Central Powers</a> in World War I.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup></p>
<p>Despite initial success, it was eventually overpowered by the Central Powers in 1915. Most of its army and some people <a href="/wiki/Serbian_army%27s_retreat_through_Albania" title="Serbian army's retreat through Albania">fled through Albania</a> to Greece and <a href="/wiki/Corfu" title="Corfu">Corfu</a>, suffering immense losses on the way. Serbia was occupied by the Central Powers. After the Central Powers military situation on other fronts worsened, the remains of the Serb army returned east and lead a final breakthrough through enemy lines on 15 September 1918, liberating Serbia and defeating the Austro-Hungarian Empire and <a href="/wiki/Bulgaria" title="Bulgaria">Bulgaria</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> Serbia, with its <a href="/wiki/Serbian_Campaign_(World_War_I)" class="mw-redirect" title="Serbian Campaign (World War I)">campaign</a>, was a major Balkan Entente Power<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> which contributed significantly to the Allied victory in the Balkans in November 1918, especially by helping France force Bulgaria's <a href="/wiki/Capitulation_(surrender)" title="Capitulation (surrender)">capitulation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> Serbia was classified as a <i>minor Entente power</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-firstworldwar.com_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-firstworldwar.com-50">[50]</a></sup></p>
<p>Serbia's casualties accounted for 8% of the total Entente military deaths; 58% (243,600) soldiers of the Serbian army perished in the war.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> The total number of casualties is placed around 700,000,<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> more than 16% of Serbia's prewar size,<sup id="cite_ref-The_Balkan_Wars_and_World_War_I_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Balkan_Wars_and_World_War_I-53">[53]</a></sup> and a majority (57%) of its overall male population.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> As the Austro-Hungarian Empire collapsed, the territory of Syrmia united with Serbia on 24 November 1918, followed by <a href="/wiki/Banat,_Ba%C4%8Dka_and_Baranja" title="Banat, Bačka and Baranja">Banat, Bačka and Baranja</a> a day later, thereby bringing the entire Vojvodina into the Serb Kingdom. On 26 November 1918, the <a href="/wiki/Podgorica_Assembly" title="Podgorica Assembly">Podgorica Assembly</a> deposed the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Petrovi%C4%87-Njego%C5%A1" class="mw-redirect" title="House of Petrović-Njegoš">House of Petrović-Njegoš</a> and united Montenegro with Serbia.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> On 1 December 1918, at <a href="/wiki/Krsmanovi%C4%87%27s_House_at_Terazije" title="Krsmanović's House at Terazije">Krsmanović's House at Terazije</a>, Serbian Prince Regent <a href="/wiki/Alexander_I_of_Yugoslavia" title="Alexander I of Yugoslavia">Alexander of Serbia</a> proclaimed the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_the_Serbs,_Croats,_and_Slovenes" class="mw-redirect" title="Kingdom of the Serbs, Croats, and Slovenes">Kingdom of the Serbs, Croats, and Slovenes</a><sup id="cite_ref-CPB_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CPB-57">[57]</a></sup> under King <a href="/wiki/Peter_I_of_Serbia" title="Peter I of Serbia">Peter I of Serbia</a>.</p>
<p>King Peter was succeeded by his son, Alexander, in August 1921. Serb centralists and Croat autonomists clashed in the parliament, and most governments were fragile and short-lived. <a href="/wiki/Nikola_Pa%C5%A1i%C4%87" title="Nikola Pašić">Nikola Pašić</a>, a conservative prime minister, headed or dominated most governments until his death. King Alexander changed the name of the country to Yugoslavia and changed the internal divisions from the 33 <a href="/wiki/Oblasts" class="mw-redirect" title="Oblasts">oblasts</a> to nine new <a href="/wiki/Subdivisions_of_the_Kingdom_of_Yugoslavia" title="Subdivisions of the Kingdom of Yugoslavia">banovinas</a>. The effect of Alexander's dictatorship was to further alienate the non-Serbs from the idea of unity.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup></p>
<p>Alexander was assassinated in <a href="/wiki/Marseille" title="Marseille">Marseille</a>, during an official visit in 1934 by <a href="/wiki/Vlado_Chernozemski" title="Vlado Chernozemski">Vlado Chernozemski</a>, member of the <a href="/wiki/Internal_Macedonian_Revolutionary_Organization" title="Internal Macedonian Revolutionary Organization">IMRO</a>. Alexander was succeeded by his eleven-year-old son <a href="/wiki/Peter_II_of_Yugoslavia" title="Peter II of Yugoslavia">Peter II</a> and a regency council was headed by his cousin, <a href="/wiki/Prince_Paul_of_Yugoslavia" title="Prince Paul of Yugoslavia">Prince Paul</a>. In August 1939 the <a href="/wiki/Cvetkovi%C4%87%E2%80%93Ma%C4%8Dek_Agreement" title="Cvetković–Maček Agreement">Cvetković–Maček Agreement</a> established an autonomous <a href="/wiki/Banate_of_Croatia" class="mw-redirect" title="Banate of Croatia">Banate of Croatia</a> as a solution to Croatian concerns.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
