</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="World_War_II_and_the_Second_Yugoslavia">World War II and the Second Yugoslavia</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/World_War_II_in_Yugoslavia" title="World War II in Yugoslavia">World War II in Yugoslavia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Socialist_Federal_Republic_of_Yugoslavia" title="Socialist Federal Republic of Yugoslavia">Socialist Federal Republic of Yugoslavia</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Invasion_of_Yugoslavia" title="Invasion of Yugoslavia">Invasion of Yugoslavia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Axis_occupation_of_Serbia" title="Axis occupation of Serbia">Axis occupation of Serbia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/World_War_II_persecution_of_Serbs" title="World War II persecution of Serbs">World War II persecution of Serbs</a></div>
<p>In 1941, in spite of Yugoslav attempts to remain neutral in the war, the <a href="/wiki/Axis_powers" title="Axis powers">Axis powers</a> invaded Yugoslavia. The territory of modern Serbia was divided between Hungary, Bulgaria, Independent State of Croatia (NDH) and Italy (greater Albania and Montenegro), while the remaining part of Serbia was placed under <a href="/wiki/Military_Administration_in_Serbia" class="mw-redirect" title="Military Administration in Serbia">German Military administration</a>, with Serbian puppet governments led by <a href="/wiki/Milan_A%C4%87imovi%C4%87" title="Milan Aćimović">Milan Aćimović</a> and <a href="/wiki/Milan_Nedi%C4%87" title="Milan Nedić">Milan Nedić</a>. The occupied territory was the scene of a civil war between <a href="/wiki/Chetniks" title="Chetniks">royalist Chetniks</a> commanded by <a href="/wiki/Dra%C5%BEa_Mihailovi%C4%87" title="Draža Mihailović">Draža Mihailović</a> and <a href="/wiki/Partisans_(Yugoslavia)" class="mw-redirect" title="Partisans (Yugoslavia)">communist partisans</a> commanded by <a href="/wiki/Josip_Broz_Tito" title="Josip Broz Tito">Josip Broz Tito</a>. Against these forces were arrayed Axis auxiliary units of the <a href="/wiki/Serbian_Volunteer_Corps_(World_War_II)" title="Serbian Volunteer Corps (World War II)">Serbian Volunteer Corps</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Serbian_State_Guard" title="Serbian State Guard">Serbian State Guard</a>. <a href="/wiki/Loznica" title="Loznica">Draginac and Loznica massacre</a> of 2,950 villagers in Western Serbia in 1941 was the first large execution of civilians in occupied Serbia by <a href="/wiki/Nazi" class="mw-redirect" title="Nazi">Germans</a>, with <a href="/wiki/Kragujevac_massacre" title="Kragujevac massacre">Kragujevac massacre</a> and <a href="/wiki/Novi_Sad_Raid" class="mw-redirect" title="Novi Sad Raid">Novi Sad Raid</a> of Jews and Serbs by Hungarian fascists being the most notorious, with over 3,000 victims in each case.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> After one year of occupation, around 16,000 <a href="/wiki/Serbian_Jews" class="mw-redirect" title="Serbian Jews">Serbian Jews</a> were murdered in the area, or around 90% of its pre-war Jewish population. Many concentration camps were established across the area. <a href="/wiki/Banjica_concentration_camp" title="Banjica concentration camp">Banjica concentration camp</a> was the largest concentration camp, with primary victims being Serbian Jews, <a href="/wiki/Romani_people" title="Romani people">Roma</a>, and Serb political prisoners.<sup id="cite_ref-JewishHeritage_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JewishHeritage-62">[62]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Fascist_occupation_of_yugoslavia.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Fascist_occupation_of_yugoslavia.png/250px-Fascist_occupation_of_yugoslavia.png" width="250" height="288" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Fascist_occupation_of_yugoslavia.png/375px-Fascist_occupation_of_yugoslavia.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Fascist_occupation_of_yugoslavia.png/500px-Fascist_occupation_of_yugoslavia.png 2x" data-file-width="1076" data-file-height="1239" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Fascist_occupation_of_yugoslavia.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Serbia (right) occupied by <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">Germany</a>, <a href="/wiki/Italian_Empire" title="Italian Empire">Italy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hungary" title="Hungary">Hungary</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bulgarian_Empire" title="Bulgarian Empire">Bulgaria</a> and <a href="/wiki/Independent_State_of_Croatia" title="Independent State of Croatia">Croatia</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>During this period, hundreds of thousands of Serbs fled the Axis <a href="/wiki/Puppet_state" title="Puppet state">puppet state</a> known as the <a href="/wiki/Independent_State_of_Croatia" title="Independent State of Croatia">Independent State of Croatia</a> and sought refuge in Serbia, seeking to escape the large-scale persecution and genocide of Serbs, Jews, and Roma being committed by the <a href="/wiki/Usta%C5%A1e" title="Ustaše">Ustaše</a> regime.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_U%C5%BEice" title="Republic of Užice">Republic of Užice</a> was a short-lived liberated territory established by the <a href="/wiki/Yugoslav_Partisans" title="Yugoslav Partisans">Partisans</a> and the first liberated territory in World War II Europe, organized as a military mini-state that existed in the autumn of 1941 in the west of <a href="/wiki/Serbia_under_German_occupation" class="mw-redirect" title="Serbia under German occupation">occupied Serbia</a>. By late 1944, the <a href="/wiki/Belgrade_Offensive" title="Belgrade Offensive">Belgrade Offensive</a> swung in favour of the partisans in the civil war; the partisans subsequently gained control of Yugoslavia.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> Following the Belgrade Offensive, the <a href="/wiki/Syrmian_Front" title="Syrmian Front">Syrmian Front</a> was the last major military action of World War II in Serbia.</p>
<p>The victory of the Communist Partisans resulted in the abolition of the monarchy and a subsequent constitutional referendum. A <a href="/wiki/One-party_state" title="One-party state">one-party state</a> was soon established in Yugoslavia by the <a href="/wiki/League_of_Communists_of_Yugoslavia" title="League of Communists of Yugoslavia">League of Communists of Yugoslavia</a>, between 60,000 and 70,000 people were killed in Serbia during the communist takeover.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> All opposition was suppressed and people deemed to be promoting opposition to socialism or promoting separatism were imprisoned or executed for sedition. Serbia became a <a href="/wiki/Constituent_state" title="Constituent state">constituent republic</a> within the <a href="/wiki/Socialist_Federal_Republic_of_Yugoslavia" title="Socialist Federal Republic of Yugoslavia">SFRY</a> known as the <a href="/wiki/Socialist_Republic_of_Serbia" title="Socialist Republic of Serbia">Socialist Republic of Serbia</a>, and had a republic-branch of the federal communist party, the <a href="/wiki/League_of_Communists_of_Serbia" title="League of Communists of Serbia">League of Communists of Serbia</a>.</p>
<p>Serbia's most powerful and influential politician in Tito-era Yugoslavia was <a href="/wiki/Aleksandar_Rankovi%C4%87" title="Aleksandar Ranković">Aleksandar Ranković</a>, one of the "big four" Yugoslav leaders, alongside Tito, <a href="/wiki/Edvard_Kardelj" title="Edvard Kardelj">Edvard Kardelj</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Milovan_%C4%90ilas" class="mw-redirect" title="Milovan Đilas">Milovan Đilas</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1945_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1945-66">[66]</a></sup> Ranković was later removed from the office because of the disagreements regarding Kosovo's <a href="/wiki/Nomenklatura" title="Nomenklatura">nomenklatura</a> and the unity of Serbia.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1945_66-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1945-66">[66]</a></sup> Ranković's dismissal was highly unpopular among Serbs.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated3_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated3-67">[67]</a></sup> Pro-decentralization reformers in Yugoslavia succeeded in the late 1960s in attaining substantial decentralization of powers, creating substantial autonomy in Kosovo and Vojvodina, and recognizing a <a href="/wiki/Muslims_by_nationality_(term)" class="mw-redirect" title="Muslims by nationality (term)">Yugoslav Muslim</a> nationality.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated3_67-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated3-67">[67]</a></sup> As a result of these reforms, there was a massive overhaul of Kosovo's nomenklatura and police, that shifted from being Serb-dominated to ethnic Albanian-dominated through firing Serbs on a large scale.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated3_67-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated3-67">[67]</a></sup> Further concessions were made to the ethnic Albanians of Kosovo in response to unrest, including the creation of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Pristina_(1969%E2%80%931999)" class="mw-redirect" title="University of Pristina (1969–1999)">University of Pristina</a> as an <a href="/wiki/Albanian_language" title="Albanian language">Albanian language</a> institution.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated3_67-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated3-67">[67]</a></sup> These changes created widespread fear among Serbs of being treated as <a href="/wiki/Second-class_citizen" title="Second-class citizen">second-class citizens</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Breakup_of_Yugoslavia_and_political_transition">Breakup of Yugoslavia and political transition</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Breakup_of_Yugoslavia" title="Breakup of Yugoslavia">Breakup of Yugoslavia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yugoslav_Wars" title="Yugoslav Wars">Yugoslav Wars</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kosovo_War" title="Kosovo War">Kosovo War</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Serbia_(1992%E2%80%932006)" title="Republic of Serbia (1992–2006)">Republic of Serbia (1992–2006)</a></div>
<p>In 1989, <a href="/wiki/Slobodan_Milo%C5%A1evi%C4%87" title="Slobodan Milošević">Slobodan Milošević</a> rose to power in Serbia. Milošević promised a reduction of powers for the autonomous provinces of Kosovo and Vojvodina, where his allies subsequently took over power, during the <a href="/wiki/Anti-bureaucratic_revolution" title="Anti-bureaucratic revolution">Anti-bureaucratic revolution</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> This ignited tensions between the communist leadership of the other republics, and awoke nationalism across the country that eventually resulted in its <a href="/wiki/Breakup_of_Yugoslavia" title="Breakup of Yugoslavia">breakup</a>, with <a href="/wiki/Slovenia" title="Slovenia">Slovenia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Croatia" title="Croatia">Croatia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Bosnia and Herzegovina">Bosnia and Herzegovina</a>, <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Macedonia" title="Republic of Macedonia">Macedonia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kosovo" title="Kosovo">Kosovo</a> declaring independence.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:NOTRS" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:NOTRS"><span title="This claim needs references to better sources. (March 2017)">better&#160;source&#160;needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Serbia and Montenegro remained together as the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Republic_of_Yugoslavia" class="mw-redirect" title="Federal Republic of Yugoslavia">Federal Republic of Yugoslavia</a> (FRY).</p>
<p>Fueled by ethnic tensions, the <a href="/wiki/Yugoslav_Wars" title="Yugoslav Wars">Yugoslav Wars</a> erupted, with the most severe conflicts taking place in <a href="/wiki/War_in_Croatia" class="mw-redirect" title="War in Croatia">Croatia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bosnian_War" title="Bosnian War">Bosnia</a>, where the large ethnic Serb communities opposed independence from Yugoslavia. The FRY remained outside the conflicts, but provided logistic, military and financial support to Serb forces in the wars. In response, the UN imposed <a href="/wiki/Sanctions_against_Serbia" class="mw-redirect" title="Sanctions against Serbia">sanctions</a> against Serbia which led to political isolation and the collapse of the economy (GDP was $24 billion in 1990 to under $10 billion in 1993).</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Former_Yugoslavia_wartime.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Former_Yugoslavia_wartime.png/250px-Former_Yugoslavia_wartime.png" width="250" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Former_Yugoslavia_wartime.png/375px-Former_Yugoslavia_wartime.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Former_Yugoslavia_wartime.png/500px-Former_Yugoslavia_wartime.png 2x" data-file-width="1887" data-file-height="1242" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Former_Yugoslavia_wartime.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Federal_Republic_of_Yugoslavia" class="mw-redirect" title="Federal Republic of Yugoslavia">Federal Republic of Yugoslavia</a> and territories of Serb breakaway states (<a href="/wiki/Republika_Srpska" title="Republika Srpska">Republika Srpska</a> and <a href="/wiki/Republika_Srpska_Krajina" class="mw-redirect" title="Republika Srpska Krajina">Republika Srpska Krajina</a>) during the <a href="/wiki/Yugoslav_wars" class="mw-redirect" title="Yugoslav wars">Yugoslav wars</a> (1991–95).</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Multi-party democracy was introduced in Serbia in 1990, officially dismantling the one-party system. Critics of Milošević claimed that the government continued to be authoritarian despite constitutional changes, as Milošević maintained strong political influence over the state media and security apparatus.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> When the ruling <a href="/wiki/Socialist_Party_of_Serbia" title="Socialist Party of Serbia">Socialist Party of Serbia</a> refused to accept its defeat in municipal elections in 1996, Serbians engaged in <a href="/wiki/1996%E2%80%931997_protests_in_Serbia" class="mw-redirect" title="1996–1997 protests in Serbia">large protests</a> against the government.</p>
<p>In 1998, peace was broken again, when the situation in Kosovo worsened with <a href="/wiki/Insurgency_in_Kosovo_(1995%E2%80%9398)" title="Insurgency in Kosovo (1995–98)">continued clashes</a> between the Albanian guerilla <a href="/wiki/Kosovo_Liberation_Army" title="Kosovo Liberation Army">Kosovo Liberation Army</a> and Yugoslav security forces. The confrontations led to the short <a href="/wiki/Kosovo_War" title="Kosovo War">Kosovo War</a> (1998–99), in which <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a> intervened, leading to the withdrawal of Serbian forces and the establishment of <a href="/wiki/UNMIK" class="mw-redirect" title="UNMIK">UN administration</a> in the province.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> After <a href="/wiki/Yugoslavian_general_election,_2000" title="Yugoslavian general election, 2000">presidential elections</a> in September 2000, opposition parties accused Milošević of <a href="/wiki/Electoral_fraud" title="Electoral fraud">electoral fraud</a>. A campaign of <a href="/wiki/Civil_resistance" title="Civil resistance">civil resistance</a> followed, led by the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Opposition_of_Serbia" title="Democratic Opposition of Serbia">Democratic Opposition of Serbia</a> (DOS), a broad coalition of anti-Milošević parties. This culminated on 5 October when half a million people from all over the country congregated in Belgrade, compelling Milošević to concede defeat.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Overthrow_of_Slobodan_Milo%C5%A1evi%C4%87" title="Overthrow of Slobodan Milošević">fall of Milošević</a> ended Yugoslavia's <a href="/wiki/International_isolation" title="International isolation">international isolation</a>. Milošević was sent to the <a href="/wiki/International_Criminal_Tribunal_for_the_former_Yugoslavia" title="International Criminal Tribunal for the former Yugoslavia">International Criminal Tribunal for the former Yugoslavia</a>. The DOS announced that FR Yugoslavia would seek to join the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>. In 2003, the Federal Republic of Yugoslavia was renamed <a href="/wiki/Serbia_and_Montenegro" title="Serbia and Montenegro">Serbia and Montenegro</a>; the EU opened negotiations with the country for the <a href="/wiki/Stabilization_and_Association_Agreement" class="mw-redirect" title="Stabilization and Association Agreement">Stabilization and Association Agreement</a>. Serbia's political climate remained tense and in 2003, the prime minister <a href="/wiki/Zoran_%C4%90in%C4%91i%C4%87" title="Zoran Đinđić">Zoran Đinđić</a> was <a href="/wiki/Assassination_of_Zoran_%C4%90in%C4%91i%C4%87" title="Assassination of Zoran Đinđić">assassinated</a> as result of a plot originating from circles of organized crime and former security officials.</p>
<p>On 21 May 2006, Montenegro held a referendum to determine whether to end its union with Serbia. The results showed 55.4% of voters in favor of independence, which was just above the 55% required by the referendum. On 5 June 2006, the <a href="/wiki/National_Assembly_of_Serbia" class="mw-redirect" title="National Assembly of Serbia">National Assembly of Serbia</a> declared Serbia to be the legal successor to the former state union.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> The Assembly of Kosovo unilaterally declared independence from Serbia on 17 February 2008. Serbia immediately condemned the declaration and continues to deny any statehood to Kosovo. The declaration has sparked varied responses from the international community, some welcoming it, while others condemned the unilateral move.<sup id="cite_ref-New_York_Sun_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-New_York_Sun-76">[76]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Belgrade-Pristina_negotiations" class="mw-redirect" title="Belgrade-Pristina negotiations">Status-neutral talks</a> between Serbia and Kosovo-Albanian authorities are held in <a href="/wiki/Brussels" title="Brussels">Brussels</a>, mediated by the EU.</p>
<p>In April 2008 Serbia was invited to join the <a href="/wiki/Intensified_Dialogue" class="mw-redirect" title="Intensified Dialogue">Intensified Dialogue</a> programme with <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a> despite the diplomatic rift with the alliance over Kosovo.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> Serbia officially applied for membership in the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> on 22 December 2009,<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> and received candidate status on 1 March 2012, following a delay in December 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc-11">[11]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> Following a positive recommendation of the <a href="/wiki/European_Commission" title="European Commission">European Commission</a> and <a href="/wiki/European_Council" title="European Council">European Council</a> in June 2013, negotiations to join the EU commenced in January 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Serbia" title="Geography of Serbia">Geography of Serbia</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:332px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Serbien_topo.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Serbien_topo.png/330px-Serbien_topo.png" width="330" height="303" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Serbien_topo.png/495px-Serbien_topo.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Serbien_topo.png/660px-Serbien_topo.png 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="1100" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Serbien_topo.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Topographic map of Serbia</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Located at the crossroads between Central<sup id="cite_ref-Serbia:_On_the_Way_to_EU_Accession_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Serbia:_On_the_Way_to_EU_Accession-13">[13]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> and Southern Europe, Serbia is found in the <a href="/wiki/Balkan_peninsula" class="mw-redirect" title="Balkan peninsula">Balkan peninsula</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Pannonian_Plain" class="mw-redirect" title="Pannonian Plain">Pannonian Plain</a>. Serbia lies between latitudes <a href="/wiki/41st_parallel_north" title="41st parallel north">41°</a> and <a href="/wiki/47th_parallel_north" title="47th parallel north">47° N</a>, and longitudes <a href="/wiki/18th_meridian_east" title="18th meridian east">18°</a> and <a href="/wiki/23rd_meridian_east" title="23rd meridian east">23° E</a>. The country covers a total of 88,361&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (including Kosovo), which places it at <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_and_outlying_territories_by_area" class="mw-redirect" title="List of countries and outlying territories by area">113th</a> place in the world; with Kosovo excluded, the total area is 77,474&#160;km<sup>2</sup>,<sup id="cite_ref-cia_profile_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia_profile-1">[1]</a></sup> which would make it 117th. Its total border length amounts to 2,027&#160;km (Albania 115&#160;km, Bosnia and Herzegovina 302&#160;km, Bulgaria 318&#160;km, Croatia 241&#160;km, Hungary 151&#160;km, Macedonia 221&#160;km, Montenegro 203&#160;km and Romania 476&#160;km).<sup id="cite_ref-cia_profile_1-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia_profile-1">[1]</a></sup> All of Kosovo's border with Albania (115&#160;km), Macedonia (159&#160;km) and Montenegro (79&#160;km)<sup id="cite_ref-cia_kosovo_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia_kosovo-83">[83]</a></sup> are under control of the Kosovo border police.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> Serbia treats the 352&#160;km long border between Kosovo and rest of Serbia as an "administrative line"; it is under shared control of Kosovo border police and Serbian police forces, and there are 11 crossing points.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Pannonian_Basin" title="Pannonian Basin">Pannonian Plain</a> covers the northern third of the country (<a href="/wiki/Vojvodina" title="Vojvodina">Vojvodina</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ma%C4%8Dva" title="Mačva">Mačva</a><sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup>) while the easternmost tip of Serbia extends into the <a href="/wiki/Wallachian_Plain" title="Wallachian Plain">Wallachian Plain</a>. The terrain of the central part of the country, with the region of <a href="/wiki/%C5%A0umadija" title="Šumadija">Šumadija</a> at its heart, consists chiefly of hills traversed by rivers. Mountains dominate the southern third of Serbia. <a href="/wiki/Dinaric_Alps" title="Dinaric Alps">Dinaric Alps</a> stretch in the west and the southwest, following the flow of the rivers <a href="/wiki/Drina" title="Drina">Drina</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ibar_(river)" title="Ibar (river)">Ibar</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Carpathian_Mountains" title="Carpathian Mountains">Carpathian Mountains</a> and <a href="/wiki/Balkan_Mountains" title="Balkan Mountains">Balkan Mountains</a> stretch in a north–south direction in eastern Serbia.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup></p>
<p>Ancient mountains in the southeast corner of the country belong to the <a href="/wiki/Rhodopes" class="mw-redirect" title="Rhodopes">Rilo-Rhodope Mountain</a> system. Elevation ranges from the <a href="/wiki/Mid%C5%BEor" title="Midžor">Midžor</a> peak of the Balkan Mountains at 2,169 metres (7,116 feet) (the highest peak in Serbia, excluding Kosovo) to the lowest point of just 17 metres (56 feet) near the Danube river at <a href="/wiki/Prahovo" title="Prahovo">Prahovo</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup> The largest lake is <a href="/wiki/%C4%90erdap_Lake" class="mw-redirect" title="Đerdap Lake">Đerdap Lake</a> (163 square kilometres or 63 square miles) and the longest river passing through Serbia is the <a href="/wiki/Danube" title="Danube">Danube</a> (587.35 kilometres or 364.96 miles).</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Climate_of_Serbia" title="Climate of Serbia">Climate of Serbia</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Veliki_Kr%C5%A1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Veliki_Kr%C5%A1.jpg/220px-Veliki_Kr%C5%A1.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Veliki_Kr%C5%A1.jpg/330px-Veliki_Kr%C5%A1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Veliki_Kr%C5%A1.jpg/440px-Veliki_Kr%C5%A1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3072" data-file-height="2304" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Veliki_Kr%C5%A1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Veliki_Kr%C5%A1" title="Veliki Krš">Veliki Krš</a>, part of <a href="/wiki/Serbian_Carpathians" title="Serbian Carpathians">Serbian Carpathians</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The climate of Serbia is under the influences of the landmass of Eurasia and the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic Ocean</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Sea" title="Mediterranean Sea">Mediterranean Sea</a>. With mean January temperatures around 0&#160;°C (32&#160;°F), and mean July temperatures of 22&#160;°C (72&#160;°F), it can be classified as a <a href="/wiki/Humid_continental_climate" title="Humid continental climate">warm-humid continental</a> or <a href="/wiki/Humid_subtropical_climate" title="Humid subtropical climate">humid subtropical climate</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> In the north, the climate is more continental, with cold winters, and hot, humid summers along with well distributed rainfall patterns. In the south, summers and autumns are drier, and winters are relatively cold, with heavy inland snowfall in the mountains.</p>
<p>Differences in elevation, proximity to the Adriatic Sea and large river basins, as well as exposure to the winds account for climate variations.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> Southern Serbia is subject to Mediterranean influences.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup> The Dinaric Alps and other mountain ranges contribute to the cooling of most of the warm air masses. Winters are quite harsh in the <a href="/wiki/Pe%C5%A1ter" title="Pešter">Pešter</a> plateau, because of the mountains which encircle it.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> One of the climatic features of Serbia is <a href="/wiki/Ko%C5%A1ava_(wind)" title="Košava (wind)">Košava</a>, a cold and very <a href="/wiki/Squall" title="Squall">squally</a> southeastern wind which starts in the <a href="/wiki/Carpathian_Mountains" title="Carpathian Mountains">Carpathian Mountains</a> and follows the <a href="/wiki/Danube" title="Danube">Danube</a> northwest through the <a href="/wiki/Iron_Gate_(Danube)" class="mw-redirect" title="Iron Gate (Danube)">Iron Gate</a> where it gains a <a href="/wiki/Mountain_jet" title="Mountain jet">jet effect</a> and continues to <a href="/wiki/Belgrade" title="Belgrade">Belgrade</a> and can spread as far south as <a href="/wiki/Ni%C5%A1" title="Niš">Niš</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-AMS_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AMS-93">[93]</a></sup></p>
<p>The average annual air temperature for the period 1961–1990 for the area with an altitude of up to 300&#160;m (984&#160;ft) is 10.9&#160;°C (51.6&#160;°F). The areas with an altitude of 300 to 500&#160;m (984 to 1,640&#160;ft) have an average annual temperature of around 10.0&#160;°C (50.0&#160;°F), and over 1,000&#160;m (3,281&#160;ft) of altitude around 6.0&#160;°C (42.8&#160;°F).<sup id="cite_ref-RHMZ_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RHMZ-94">[94]</a></sup> The lowest recorded temperature in Serbia was −39.5&#160;°C (−39.1&#160;°F) on 13 January 1985, <a href="/wiki/Karajuki%C4%87a_Bunari" title="Karajukića Bunari">Karajukića Bunari</a> in Pešter, and the highest was 44.9&#160;°C or 112.8&#160;°F, on 24 July 2007, recorded in <a href="/wiki/Smederevska_Palanka" title="Smederevska Palanka">Smederevska Palanka</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-95">[95]</a></sup></p>
<p>Serbia is one of few European countries with <i>very high risk</i> exposure to natural hazards (earthquakes, storms, floods, droughts).<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup> It is estimated that potential floods, particularly in areas of Central Serbia, threaten over 500 larger settlements and an area of 16,000 square kilometers.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup> The most disastrous were the <a href="/wiki/2014_Southeast_Europe_floods" title="2014 Southeast Europe floods">floods in May 2014</a>, when 57 people died and a damage of over a 1.5 billion euro was inflicted.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hydrology">Hydrology</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/List_of_rivers_of_Serbia" title="List of rivers of Serbia">List of rivers of Serbia</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_lakes_of_Serbia" title="List of lakes of Serbia">List of lakes of Serbia</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Veliki_Kazan.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Veliki_Kazan.jpg/220px-Veliki_Kazan.jpg" width="220" height="127" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Veliki_Kazan.jpg/330px-Veliki_Kazan.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Veliki_Kazan.jpg/440px-Veliki_Kazan.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5000" data-file-height="2887" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Veliki_Kazan.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Iron_Gates" title="Iron Gates">Iron Gates</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Almost all of Serbia's rivers drain to the <a href="/wiki/Black_Sea" title="Black Sea">Black Sea</a>, by way of the Danube river. The <a href="/wiki/Danube" title="Danube">Danube</a>, the second largest European river, passes through Serbia with 588 kilometers (21% of its overall length) and represents the largest source of fresh water. It is joined by its biggest tributaries, the <a href="/wiki/Great_Morava" title="Great Morava">Great Morava</a> (longest river entirely in Serbia with 493&#160;km of length), <a href="/wiki/Sava" title="Sava">Sava</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tisza" title="Tisza">Tisza</a> rivers.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> One notable exception is the <a href="/wiki/P%C4%8Dinja_(river)" title="Pčinja (river)">Pčinja</a> which flows into the <a href="/wiki/Aegean_Sea" title="Aegean Sea">Aegean</a>. <a href="/wiki/Drina" title="Drina">Drina</a> river forms the natural border between <a href="/wiki/Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Bosnia and Herzegovina">Bosnia and Herzegovina</a> and Serbia, and represents the main <a href="/wiki/Kayaking" title="Kayaking">kayaking</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rafting" title="Rafting">rafting</a> attraction in both countries.</p>
<p>Due to configuration of the terrain, natural lakes are sparse and small; most of them are located in the lowlands of Vojvodina, like the aeolian lake <a href="/wiki/Pali%C4%87_lake" class="mw-redirect" title="Palić lake">Palić</a> or numerous <a href="/wiki/Oxbow_lake" title="Oxbow lake">oxbow lakes</a> along river flows (like <a href="/wiki/Zasavica_(river)" title="Zasavica (river)">Zasavica</a> and <a href="/wiki/Carska_Bara" title="Carska Bara">Carska Bara</a>). However, there are numerous <a href="/wiki/Artificial_lake" class="mw-redirect" title="Artificial lake">artificial lakes</a>, mostly due to hydroelectric dams, the biggest being <a href="/wiki/Iron_Gate_(Danube)" class="mw-redirect" title="Iron Gate (Danube)">Đerdap (Iron Gates)</a> on the Danube with 163&#160;km<sup>2</sup> on the Serbian side (a total area of 253&#160;km<sup>2</sup> is shared with Romania) as well as the deepest (with maximum depth of 92 m); <a href="/wiki/Peru%C4%87ac" title="Perućac">Perućac</a> on the Drina, and <a href="/wiki/Vlasina_Lake" title="Vlasina Lake">Vlasina</a>. The largest waterfall, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Jelovarnik&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Jelovarnik (page does not exist)">Jelovarnik</a>, located in Kopaonik, is 71 m high.<sup id="cite_ref-pod2.stat.gov.rs_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pod2.stat.gov.rs-100">[100]</a></sup> Abundance of relatively unpolluted surface waters and numerous underground natural and mineral water sources of high <a href="/wiki/Water_quality" title="Water quality">water quality</a> presents a chance for export and economy improvement; however, more extensive exploitation and production of bottled water began only recently.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Environment">Environment</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_protected_natural_resources_in_Serbia" title="List of protected natural resources in Serbia">List of protected natural resources in Serbia</a></div>
<p>With 29.1% of its territory covered by forest, Serbia is considered to be a middle-forested country, compared on a global scale to world forest coverage at 30%, and European average of 35%. The total forest area in Serbia is 2,252,000 ha (1,194,000 ha or 53% are state-owned, and 1,058,387 ha or 47% are privately owned) or 0.3 ha per inhabitant.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup> The most common trees are oak, beech, pines and firs.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Uvac_River_and_Eagle.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Uvac_River_and_Eagle.jpg/220px-Uvac_River_and_Eagle.jpg" width="220" height="105" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Uvac_River_and_Eagle.jpg/330px-Uvac_River_and_Eagle.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Uvac_River_and_Eagle.jpg/440px-Uvac_River_and_Eagle.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3101" data-file-height="1473" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Uvac_River_and_Eagle.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Uvac" title="Uvac">Uvac Gorge</a> is considered one of the last habitats of the <a href="/wiki/Griffon_vulture" title="Griffon vulture">griffon vulture</a> in Europe<a href="/wiki/Griffon_vulture" title="Griffon vulture">Griffon vulture</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Serbia is a country of rich ecosystem and species diversity – covering only 1.9% of the whole European territory Serbia is home to 39% of European vascular flora, 51% of European fish fauna, 40% of European reptile and amphibian fauna, 74% of European bird fauna, 67% European mammal fauna.<sup id="cite_ref-iucn.org_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-iucn.org-102">[102]</a></sup> Its abundance of mountains and rivers make it an ideal environment for a variety of animals, many of which are protected including wolves, lynx, bears, foxes and stags. There are 17 snake species living all over the country, 8 of them are venomous.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup> Serbia is home to highly protected owl species. In the northernmost part of <a href="/wiki/Vojvodina" title="Vojvodina">Vojvodina</a> plain, in the city of <a href="/wiki/Kikinda" title="Kikinda">Kikinda</a>, a number of endangered 145 <a href="/wiki/Long-eared_owl" title="Long-eared owl">long-eared owls</a> is noted, making this town the world's biggest settlement of these species.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup> Serbia is considerably rich with threatened species of bats and butterflies.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup></p>
<p>Mountain of <a href="/wiki/Tara_(mountain)" title="Tara (mountain)">Tara</a> in western Serbia is one of the last regions in Europe where bears can still live in absolute freedom.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup> Serbia is also home to about 380 species of bird. In <a href="/wiki/Carska_Bara" title="Carska Bara">Carska Bara</a>, there are over 300 bird species on just a few square kilometers.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Uvac" title="Uvac">Uvac Gorge</a> is considered one of the last habitats of the <a href="/wiki/Griffon_vulture" title="Griffon vulture">griffon vulture</a> in Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup></p>
<p>There are 377 <a href="/wiki/List_of_protected_natural_resources_in_Serbia" title="List of protected natural resources in Serbia">protected areas of Serbia</a>, encompassing 4,947 square kilometers or 6.4% of the country. The "Spatial plan of the Republic of Serbia" states that the total protected area should be increased to 12% by 2021.<sup id="cite_ref-iucn.org_102-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-iucn.org-102">[102]</a></sup> Those protected areas include 5 national parks (<a href="/wiki/%C4%90erdap_National_Park" class="mw-redirect" title="Đerdap National Park">Đerdap</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tara_(mountain)" title="Tara (mountain)">Tara</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kopaonik" title="Kopaonik">Kopaonik</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fru%C5%A1ka_Gora" title="Fruška Gora">Fruška Gora</a> and <a href="/wiki/%C5%A0ar_Mountain" class="mw-redirect" title="Šar Mountain">Šar Mountain</a>), 15 <a href="/wiki/Nature_park" title="Nature park">nature parks</a>, 15 "landscapes of outstanding features", 61 nature reserves, and 281 natural monuments.<sup id="cite_ref-pod2.stat.gov.rs_100-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pod2.stat.gov.rs-100">[100]</a></sup></p>
<p>Air pollution is a significant problem in <a href="/wiki/Bor,_Serbia" title="Bor, Serbia">Bor</a> area, due to work of large copper mining and smelting complex, and <a href="/wiki/Pan%C4%8Devo" title="Pančevo">Pančevo</a> where oil and petrochemical industry is based.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup> Some cities suffer from water supply problems, due to mismanagement and low investments in the past, as well as water pollution (like the pollution of the <a href="/wiki/Ibar_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Ibar River">Ibar River</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Trep%C4%8Da_Mines" title="Trepča Mines">Trepča</a> <a href="/wiki/Zinc" title="Zinc">zinc</a>-lead combinate, affecting the city of <a href="/wiki/Kraljevo" title="Kraljevo">Kraljevo</a>, or the presence of natural <a href="/wiki/Arsenic" title="Arsenic">arsenic</a> in underground waters in <a href="/wiki/Zrenjanin" title="Zrenjanin">Zrenjanin</a>).</p>
<p>Poor waste management has been identified as one of the most important environmental problems in Serbia and the <a href="/wiki/Recycling" title="Recycling">recycling</a> is a fledgling activity, with only 15% of its waste being turned back for reuse.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/NATO_bombing_of_Yugoslavia" title="NATO bombing of Yugoslavia">1999 NATO bombing</a> caused serious damage to the environment, with several thousand tons of toxic chemicals stored in targeted factories and refineries released into the soil and water basins.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Serbia" title="Politics of Serbia">Politics of Serbia</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_political_parties_in_Serbia" title="List of political parties in Serbia">List of political parties in Serbia</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:%D0%94%D0%BE%D0%BC_%D0%9D%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%B4%D0%BD%D0%B5_%D0%A1%D0%BA%D1%83%D0%BF%D1%88%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%B5_%D0%A1%D1%80%D0%B1%D0%B8%D1%98%D0%B5.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/%D0%94%D0%BE%D0%BC_%D0%9D%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%B4%D0%BD%D0%B5_%D0%A1%D0%BA%D1%83%D0%BF%D1%88%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%B5_%D0%A1%D1%80%D0%B1%D0%B8%D1%98%D0%B5.jpg/300px-%D0%94%D0%BE%D0%BC_%D0%9D%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%B4%D0%BD%D0%B5_%D0%A1%D0%BA%D1%83%D0%BF%D1%88%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%B5_%D0%A1%D1%80%D0%B1%D0%B8%D1%98%D0%B5.jpg" width="300" height="126" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/%D0%94%D0%BE%D0%BC_%D0%9D%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%B4%D0%BD%D0%B5_%D0%A1%D0%BA%D1%83%D0%BF%D1%88%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%B5_%D0%A1%D1%80%D0%B1%D0%B8%D1%98%D0%B5.jpg/450px-%D0%94%D0%BE%D0%BC_%D0%9D%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%B4%D0%BD%D0%B5_%D0%A1%D0%BA%D1%83%D0%BF%D1%88%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%B5_%D0%A1%D1%80%D0%B1%D0%B8%D1%98%D0%B5.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/%D0%94%D0%BE%D0%BC_%D0%9D%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%B4%D0%BD%D0%B5_%D0%A1%D0%BA%D1%83%D0%BF%D1%88%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%B5_%D0%A1%D1%80%D0%B1%D0%B8%D1%98%D0%B5.jpg/600px-%D0%94%D0%BE%D0%BC_%D0%9D%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%B4%D0%BD%D0%B5_%D0%A1%D0%BA%D1%83%D0%BF%D1%88%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%B5_%D0%A1%D1%80%D0%B1%D0%B8%D1%98%D0%B5.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4614" data-file-height="1940" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:%D0%94%D0%BE%D0%BC_%D0%9D%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%B4%D0%BD%D0%B5_%D0%A1%D0%BA%D1%83%D0%BF%D1%88%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%B5_%D0%A1%D1%80%D0%B1%D0%B8%D1%98%D0%B5.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/House_of_the_National_Assembly_of_Serbia" title="House of the National Assembly of Serbia">House of the National Assembly</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Serbia is a <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_republic" title="Parliamentary republic">parliamentary republic</a>, with the government divided into legislative, executive and judiciary branches.</p>
<p>Serbia had one of the first modern constitutions in Europe, the 1835 Constitution (known as "Sretenje Constitution"), which was at the time considered among the most progressive and liberal constitutions in the world. Since then it has adopted 10 different constitutions.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup> The current constitution was adopted in 2006 in the aftermath of <a href="/wiki/Montenegrin_independence_referendum,_2006" title="Montenegrin independence referendum, 2006">Montenegro independence referendum</a> which by consequence renewed the independence of Serbia itself.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_Court_of_Serbia" title="Constitutional Court of Serbia">Constitutional Court</a> rules on matters regarding the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Serbia" title="Constitution of Serbia">Constitution</a>.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/President_of_Serbia" title="President of Serbia">President of the Republic</a> (<i>Predsednik Republike</i>) is the <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">head of state</a>, is elected by popular vote to a five-year term and is limited by the Constitution to a maximum of two terms. In addition to being the <a href="/wiki/Commander_in_chief" class="mw-redirect" title="Commander in chief">commander in chief</a> of the armed forces, the president has the procedural duty of appointing the prime minister with the consent of the parliament, and has some influence on foreign policy.<sup id="cite_ref-President_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-President-113">[113]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Tomislav_Nikoli%C4%87" title="Tomislav Nikolić">Tomislav Nikolić</a> is the current president following the 2012 presidential election.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup> Seat of the presidency is <a href="/wiki/Andri%C4%87ev_Venac" title="Andrićev Venac">Novi Dvor</a>.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Serbia" title="Government of Serbia">Government</a> (<i>Vlada</i>) is composed of the <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Serbia" title="Prime Minister of Serbia">prime minister</a> and cabinet ministers. The Government is responsible for proposing legislation and a budget, executing the laws, and guiding the foreign and internal policies. The current prime minister is <a href="/wiki/Ana_Brnabi%C4%87" title="Ana Brnabić">Ana Brnabić</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Serbian_Progressive_Party" title="Serbian Progressive Party">Serbian Progressive Party</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_Serbia" class="mw-redirect" title="Parliament of Serbia">National Assembly</a> (<i>Narodna skupština</i>) is a <a href="/wiki/Unicameral" class="mw-redirect" title="Unicameral">unicameral</a> legislative body. The National Assembly has the power to enact laws, approve the budget, schedule presidential elections, select and dismiss the Prime Minister and other ministers, declare war, and ratify international treaties and agreements.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup> It is composed of 250 <a href="/wiki/Proportional_representation" title="Proportional representation">proportionally</a> elected members who serve four-year terms. The largest political parties in Serbia are the centre-right <a href="/wiki/Serbian_Progressive_Party" title="Serbian Progressive Party">Serbian Progressive Party</a>, leftist <a href="/wiki/Socialist_Party_of_Serbia" title="Socialist Party of Serbia">Socialist Party of Serbia</a> and centre-left <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(Serbia)" title="Democratic Party (Serbia)">Democratic Party</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Law_and_criminal_justice">Law and criminal justice</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Law_of_Serbia" title="Law of Serbia">Law of Serbia</a></div>
<p>Serbia has a three-tiered judicial system, made up of the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_Cassation_(Serbia)" title="Supreme Court of Cassation (Serbia)">Supreme Court of Cassation</a> as the court of the last resort, <a href="/wiki/Court_of_Appeal" class="mw-redirect" title="Court of Appeal">Courts of Appeal</a> as the appellate instance, and Basic and High courts as the general jurisdictions at first instance.</p>
<p>Courts of special jurisdictions are the Administrative Court, commercial courts (including the Commercial Court of Appeal at second instance) and misdemeanor courts (including High Misdemeanor Court at second instance).<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup> The judiciary is overseen by the Ministry of Justice. Serbia has a typical <a href="/wiki/Civil_law_(legal_system)" title="Civil law (legal system)">civil law</a> legal system.</p>
<p>Law enforcement is the responsibility of the <a href="/wiki/Law_enforcement_in_Serbia" title="Law enforcement in Serbia">Serbian Police</a>, which is subordinate to the Ministry of the Interior. Serbian Police fields 26,527 uniformed officers.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup> National security and counterintelligence are the responsibility of the <a href="/wiki/Security_Information_Agency" class="mw-redirect" title="Security Information Agency">Security Information Agency (BIA)</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Serbia" title="Foreign relations of Serbia">Foreign relations of Serbia</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Accession_of_Serbia_to_the_European_Union" title="Accession of Serbia to the European Union">Accession of Serbia to the European Union</a> and <a href="/wiki/Political_status_of_Kosovo" title="Political status of Kosovo">Political status of Kosovo</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Serbian_embassies.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Serbian_embassies.png/220px-Serbian_embassies.png" width="220" height="96" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Serbian_embassies.png/330px-Serbian_embassies.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Serbian_embassies.png/440px-Serbian_embassies.png 2x" data-file-width="1425" data-file-height="625" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Serbian_embassies.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Serbian has embassies in 65 countries around the world</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Serbia has established diplomatic relations with 188 <a href="/wiki/UN_member_states" class="mw-redirect" title="UN member states">UN member states</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Holy_See" title="Holy See">Holy See</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Sovereign_Military_Order_of_Malta" title="Sovereign Military Order of Malta">Sovereign Military Order of Malta</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-DList_121-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DList-121">[121]</a></sup> Foreign relations are conducted through the Ministry of Foreign Affairs. Serbia has a network of 65 embassies and 23 consulates internationally.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup> There are 65 <a href="/wiki/List_of_diplomatic_missions_in_Serbia" title="List of diplomatic missions in Serbia">foreign embassies</a>, 5 consulates and 4 liaison offices in Serbia.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup></p>
<p>Serbian foreign policy is focused on achieving the strategic goal of becoming a <a href="/wiki/Member_state_of_the_European_Union" title="Member state of the European Union">member state of the European Union</a> (EU). Serbia started the process of joining the EU by signing of the <a href="/wiki/Stabilisation_and_Association_Process" title="Stabilisation and Association Process">Stabilisation and Association Agreement</a> on 29 April 2008 and officially applied for membership in the European Union on 22 December 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup> It received a full <a href="/wiki/Future_enlargement_of_the_European_Union#Recognised_candidates" title="Future enlargement of the European Union">candidate status</a> on 1 March 2012 and started <a href="/wiki/Enlargement_of_the_EU" class="mw-redirect" title="Enlargement of the EU">accession talks</a> on 21 January 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-Council_of_the_EU_125-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Council_of_the_EU-125">[125]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup></p>
<p>The province of <a href="/wiki/Kosovo" title="Kosovo">Kosovo</a> declared independence from Serbia on 17 February 2008, which sparked varied responses from the international community, some welcoming it, while others condemn the unilateral move.<sup id="cite_ref-New_York_Sun_76-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-New_York_Sun-76">[76]</a></sup> Serbia has, at first, recalled its ambassadors from states which have recognized <a href="/wiki/Kosovo" title="Kosovo">Kosovo</a>, in protest.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Serbian_Armed_Forces" title="Serbian Armed Forces">Serbian Armed Forces</a> and <a href="/wiki/Military_history_of_Serbia" title="Military history of Serbia">Military history of Serbia</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:MiG-29_RV_i_PVO_VS-5.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/MiG-29_RV_i_PVO_VS-5.jpg/220px-MiG-29_RV_i_PVO_VS-5.jpg" width="220" height="155" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/MiG-29_RV_i_PVO_VS-5.jpg/330px-MiG-29_RV_i_PVO_VS-5.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/MiG-29_RV_i_PVO_VS-5.jpg/440px-MiG-29_RV_i_PVO_VS-5.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2448" data-file-height="1728" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:MiG-29_RV_i_PVO_VS-5.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Serbian_Air_Force" class="mw-redirect" title="Serbian Air Force">Serbian Air Force</a> <a href="/wiki/MiG-29" class="mw-redirect" title="MiG-29">MiG-29</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Serbian Armed Forces are subordinate to the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Defence_(Serbia)" title="Ministry of Defence (Serbia)">Ministry of Defence</a>, and are composed of the <a href="/wiki/Serbian_Army" title="Serbian Army">Army</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Serbian_Air_Force_and_Air_Defence" title="Serbian Air Force and Air Defence">Air Force</a>. Although a <a href="/wiki/Landlocked_country" title="Landlocked country">landlocked country</a>, Serbia operates a <a href="/wiki/Serbian_River_Flotilla" title="Serbian River Flotilla">River Flotilla</a> which patrols on the <a href="/wiki/Danube" title="Danube">Danube</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sava" title="Sava">Sava</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tisza" title="Tisza">Tisza</a> rivers. The Serbian <a href="/wiki/Chief_of_the_General_Staff_(Serbia)" class="mw-redirect" title="Chief of the General Staff (Serbia)">Chief of the General Staff</a> reports to the Defence Minister. The Chief of Staff is appointed by the <a href="/wiki/President_of_Serbia" title="President of Serbia">President</a>, who is the <a href="/wiki/Commander-in-chief" title="Commander-in-chief">Commander-in-chief</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-President_113-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-President-113">[113]</a></sup> As of 2017<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Serbia&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, Serbia defence budget amounts to $503 million or an estimated 1.4% of the country's GDP.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup></p>
<p>Traditionally having relied on a large number of conscripts, Serbian Armed Forces went through a period of downsizing, restructuring and <a href="/wiki/Professionalisation" class="mw-redirect" title="Professionalisation">professionalisation</a>. <a href="/wiki/Conscription" title="Conscription">Conscription</a> was abolished in 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup> Serbian Armed Forces have 28,000 active troops,<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup> supplemented by the "active reserve" which numbers 20,000 members and "passive reserve" with about 170,000.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup></p>
<p>Serbia participates in the <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a> <a href="/wiki/Individual_Partnership_Action_Plan" title="Individual Partnership Action Plan">Individual Partnership Action Plan</a> program,<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup> but has shown no intention of joining <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a> in the near future, due to significant popular rejection, largely derived from the NATO bombing of Yugoslavia in 1999.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup> It is an observer member of the Collective Securities Treaty Organization (CSTO)<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup> The country also signed the <a href="/wiki/Stability_Pact_for_South_Eastern_Europe" title="Stability Pact for South Eastern Europe">Stability Pact for South Eastern Europe</a>. The Serbian Armed Forces take part in several multinational peacekeeping missions, including deployments in <a href="/wiki/Lebanon" title="Lebanon">Lebanon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cyprus" title="Cyprus">Cyprus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ivory_Coast" title="Ivory Coast">Ivory Coast</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Liberia" title="Liberia">Liberia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup></p>
<p>Serbia is a large producer and exporter of military equipment in the region. Defence exports totaled around $483 million in 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup> Serbia exports across the world, notably to the Middle East, Africa, Southeast Asia, and North America.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup> The defence industry has seen significant growth over the years and it continues to grow on a yearly basis.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Districts_of_Serbia.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Districts_of_Serbia.png/180px-Districts_of_Serbia.png" width="180" height="257" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Districts_of_Serbia.png/270px-Districts_of_Serbia.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Districts_of_Serbia.png/360px-Districts_of_Serbia.png 2x" data-file-width="1824" data-file-height="2603" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Districts_of_Serbia.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Administrative_divisions_of_Serbia" title="Administrative divisions of Serbia">Districts of Serbia</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Administrative_divisions_of_Serbia" title="Administrative divisions of Serbia">Administrative divisions of Serbia</a></div>
<p>Serbia is a <a href="/wiki/Unitary_state" title="Unitary state">unitary state</a><sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup> composed of <a href="/wiki/Municipalities_of_Serbia" class="mw-redirect" title="Municipalities of Serbia">municipalities</a>/<a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_in_Serbia" title="List of cities in Serbia">cities</a>, districts, and two autonomous provinces. In Serbia, excluding Kosovo, there are 138 municipalities (<i>opštine</i>) and 23 cities (<i>gradovi</i>), which form the basic units of local self-government.<sup id="cite_ref-zakon_142-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-zakon-142">[142]</a></sup> Apart from municipalities, there are 24 <a href="/wiki/List_of_districts_of_Serbia" title="List of districts of Serbia">districts</a> (<i>okruzi</i>), with the City of Belgrade constituting an additional district. Except for Belgrade, which has an elected local government, districts are regional centers of state authority, but have no powers of their own; they present purely administrative divisions.<sup id="cite_ref-zakon_142-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-zakon-142">[142]</a></sup></p>
<p>Serbia has two autonomous provinces, <a href="/wiki/Vojvodina" title="Vojvodina">Vojvodina</a> in the north, and <a href="/wiki/Kosovo_and_Metohija" class="mw-redirect" title="Kosovo and Metohija">Kosovo and Metohija</a> in the south,<sup id="cite_ref-zakon_142-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-zakon-142">[142]</a></sup> while the remaining area, "<a href="/wiki/Central_Serbia" title="Central Serbia">Central Serbia</a>", never had its own regional authority. Following the <a href="/wiki/Kosovo_War" title="Kosovo War">Kosovo War</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Interim_Administration_Mission_in_Kosovo" title="United Nations Interim Administration Mission in Kosovo">UN peacekeepers</a> entered Kosovo, as per <a href="/wiki/UN_Security_Council_Resolution_1244" class="mw-redirect" title="UN Security Council Resolution 1244">UNSC Resolution 1244</a>. In 2008, <a href="/wiki/2008_Kosovo_declaration_of_independence" title="2008 Kosovo declaration of independence">Kosovo declared independence</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup> The government of Serbia did not recognize the declaration, considering it illegal and illegitimate.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Serbia" title="Demographics of Serbia">Demographics of Serbia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Demographic_history_of_Serbia" title="Demographic history of Serbia">Demographic history of Serbia</a></div>
<p>As of 2011<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Serbia&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> census, Serbia (excluding Kosovo) has a total population of 7,186,862 and the overall <a href="/wiki/List_of_sovereign_states_and_dependent_territories_by_population_density" class="mw-redirect" title="List of sovereign states and dependent territories by population density">population density</a> is medium as it stands at 92.8 inhabitants per square kilometer.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup> The census was not conducted in <a href="/wiki/Kosovo" title="Kosovo">Kosovo</a> which held its own census that numbered their total population at 1,739,825,<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">[146]</a></sup> excluding Serb-inhabited <a href="/wiki/North_Kosovo" title="North Kosovo">North Kosovo</a>, as <a href="/wiki/Serbs_of_Kosovo" class="mw-redirect" title="Serbs of Kosovo">Serbs</a> from that area (about 50,000) boycotted the census.</p>

</div>
</div>
<p>Serbia has been enduring a demographic crisis since the beginning of the 1990s, with a <a href="/wiki/Death_rate" class="mw-redirect" title="Death rate">death rate</a> that has continuously exceeded its <a href="/wiki/Birth_rate" title="Birth rate">birth rate</a>, and a <a href="/wiki/Total_fertility_rate" title="Total fertility rate">total fertility rate</a> of 1.43 children per mother, one of the lowest in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">[147]</a></sup> Serbia subsequently has one of the oldest populations in the world, with the average age of 42.9 years,<sup id="cite_ref-stat.gov.rs_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stat.gov.rs-2">[2]</a></sup> and its population is shrinking at one of the fastest rates in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">[148]</a></sup> A fifth of all households consist of only one person, and just one-fourth of four and more persons.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">[149]</a></sup> Average <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_life_expectancy" title="List of countries by life expectancy">Life expectancy in Serbia</a> at birth is 74.8 years.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">[150]</a></sup></p>
<p>During the 1990s, Serbia used to have the largest refugee population in Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">[151]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Refugees" class="mw-redirect" title="Refugees">Refugees</a> and <a href="/wiki/Internally_displaced_person" title="Internally displaced person">internally displaced persons</a> (IDPs) in Serbia formed between 7% and 7.5% of its population at the time – about half a million refugees sought refuge in the country following the series of <a href="/wiki/Yugoslav_wars" class="mw-redirect" title="Yugoslav wars">Yugoslav wars</a>, mainly from Croatia (and to a lesser extent from Bosnia and Herzegovina) and the IDPs from Kosovo.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">[152]</a></sup> Meanwhile, it is estimated that 300,000 people left Serbia during the 1990s, 20% of which had a higher education.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">[153]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-survey_154-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-survey-154">[154]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Serbs" title="Serbs">Serbs</a> with 5,988,150 are the largest ethnic group in Serbia, representing 83% of the total population (excluding Kosovo). With a population of 253,899, <a href="/wiki/Hungarians_in_Serbia" title="Hungarians in Serbia">Hungarians</a> are the largest ethnic minority in Serbia, concentrated predominately in northern Vojvodina and representing 3.5% of the country's population (13% in Vojvodina). Romani population stands at 147,604 according to the 2011 census but unofficial estimates place their actual number between 400,000 and 500,000.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">[155]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Bosniaks_of_Serbia" title="Bosniaks of Serbia">Bosniaks</a> with 145,278 are concentrated in <a href="/wiki/Sand%C5%BEak" title="Sandžak">Raška (Sandžak)</a>, in the southwest. Other minority groups include <a href="/wiki/Croats_of_Serbia" title="Croats of Serbia">Croats</a>, <a href="/wiki/Slovaks_in_Serbia" title="Slovaks in Serbia">Slovaks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Albanians_in_Serbia" title="Albanians in Serbia">Albanians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Montenegrins_in_Serbia" class="mw-redirect" title="Montenegrins in Serbia">Montenegrins</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vlachs_of_Serbia" title="Vlachs of Serbia">Vlachs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Romanians_in_Serbia" class="mw-redirect" title="Romanians in Serbia">Romanians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Macedonians_in_Serbia" title="Macedonians in Serbia">Macedonians</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bulgarians_in_Serbia" title="Bulgarians in Serbia">Bulgarians</a>. <a href="/wiki/Chinese_people_in_Serbia" title="Chinese people in Serbia">Chinese</a>, estimated at about 15,000, are the only significant <a href="/wiki/Immigrant" class="mw-redirect" title="Immigrant">immigrant</a> minority.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">[156]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">[157]</a></sup></p>
<p>The majority of the population, or 59.4%, reside in urban areas and some 16.1% in Belgrade alone. Belgrade is the only city with more than a million inhabitants and there are four more with over 100,000 inhabitants.<sup id="cite_ref-census2011_158-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-census2011-158">[158]</a></sup></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Serbia" title="Religion in Serbia">Religion in Serbia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Serbian_Orthodox_Church" title="Serbian Orthodox Church">Serbian Orthodox Church</a></div>
