</div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education_and_science">Education and science</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Serbia" title="Education in Serbia">Education in Serbia</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:162px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Milutin_Milankovi%C4%87.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Milutin_Milankovi%C4%87.jpg/160px-Milutin_Milankovi%C4%87.jpg" width="160" height="286" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Milutin_Milankovi%C4%87.jpg/240px-Milutin_Milankovi%C4%87.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Milutin_Milankovi%C4%87.jpg/320px-Milutin_Milankovi%C4%87.jpg 2x" data-file-width="358" data-file-height="640" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Milutin_Milankovi%C4%87.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Milutin_Milankovi%C4%87" title="Milutin Milanković">Milutin Milanković</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mathematician" title="Mathematician">mathematician</a>, <a href="/wiki/Astronomer" title="Astronomer">astronomer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Climatologist" class="mw-redirect" title="Climatologist">climatologist</a> and <a href="/wiki/Geophysics" title="Geophysics">geophysicist</a>, ranked among the top fifteen minds of all time in the field of earth sciences.<sup id="cite_ref-229" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-229">[229]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>According to 2011 census, literacy in Serbia stands at 98% of population while computer literacy is at 49% (complete computer literacy is at 34.2%).<sup id="cite_ref-230" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-230">[230]</a></sup> Same census showed the following levels of education: 16.2% of inhabitants have higher education (10.6% have bachelors or master's degrees, 5.6% have an associate degree), 49% have a secondary education, 20.7% have an elementary education, and 13.7% have not completed elementary education.<sup id="cite_ref-231" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-231">[231]</a></sup></p>
<p>Education in Serbia is regulated by the Ministry of Education and Science. Education starts in either preschools or elementary schools. Children enroll in elementary schools at the age of seven. Compulsory education consists of eight grades of elementary school. Students have the opportunity to attend <a href="/wiki/Gymnasium_(school)" title="Gymnasium (school)">gymnasiums</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vocational_school" title="Vocational school">vocational schools</a> for another four years, or to enroll in vocational training for 2 to 3 years. Following the completion of gymnasiums or vocational schools, students have the opportunity to attend university.<sup id="cite_ref-232" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-232">[232]</a></sup> Elementary and secondary education are also available in languages of recognised minorities in Serbia, where classes are held in <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_language" title="Hungarian language">Hungarian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Slovak_language" title="Slovak language">Slovak</a>, Albanian, Romanian, <a href="/wiki/Rusyn_language" title="Rusyn language">Rusyn</a>, Bulgarian as well as Bosnian and Croatian languages.</p>
<p>There are 17 universities in Serbia (eight public universities with a total number of 85 <a href="/wiki/Faculty_(division)" title="Faculty (division)">faculties</a> and nine private universities with 51 faculties).<sup id="cite_ref-233" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-233">[233]</a></sup> In 2010/2011 academic year, 181,362 students attended 17 universities (148,248 at public universities and some 33,114 at private universities) while 47,169 attended 81 "higher schools".<sup id="cite_ref-pod2.stat.gov.rs_100-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pod2.stat.gov.rs-100">[100]</a></sup> Public universities in Serbia are: the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Belgrade" title="University of Belgrade">University of Belgrade</a> (oldest, founded in 1808, and largest university with 89,827 undergraduates and graduates<sup id="cite_ref-234" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-234">[234]</a></sup>), <a href="/wiki/University_of_Novi_Sad" title="University of Novi Sad">University of Novi Sad</a> (founded in 1960 and with student body of 47,826<sup id="cite_ref-235" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-235">[235]</a></sup>), <a href="/wiki/University_of_Ni%C5%A1" title="University of Niš">University of Niš</a> (founded in 1965; 27,000 students), <a href="/wiki/University_of_Kragujevac" title="University of Kragujevac">University of Kragujevac</a> (founded in 1976; 14,000 students), <a href="/wiki/Univerzitet_u_Pri%C5%A1tini" title="Univerzitet u Prištini">University of Priština – Kos. Mitrovica</a>, <a href="/wiki/State_University_of_Novi_Pazar" title="State University of Novi Pazar">Public University of Novi Pazar</a> as well as two specialist universities – <a href="/wiki/University_of_Arts_(Belgrade)" class="mw-redirect" title="University of Arts (Belgrade)">University of Arts</a> and <a href="/wiki/Military_Academy_(Serbia)" title="Military Academy (Serbia)">University of Defence</a>. Largest private universities include <a href="/wiki/John_Naisbitt_University" title="John Naisbitt University">John Naisbitt University</a> and <a href="/wiki/Singidunum_University" title="Singidunum University">Singidunum University</a>, both in Belgrade, and Educons University in Novi Sad. Public universities tend to be of a better quality and therefore more renowned than private ones. The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Belgrade" title="University of Belgrade">University of Belgrade</a> (placed in 301–400 bracket on <a href="/wiki/Academic_Ranking_of_World_Universities" title="Academic Ranking of World Universities">2013 Shanghai Ranking of World Universities</a>, being best-placed university in Southeast Europe after those in Athens and Thessaloniki) and <a href="/wiki/University_of_Novi_Sad" title="University of Novi Sad">University of Novi Sad</a> are generally considered as the best institutions of higher learning in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-236" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-236">[236]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tmulti tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:204px;max-width:204px">
<div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Narodna_biblioteka_i_Hram_Sv._Save.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Narodna_biblioteka_i_Hram_Sv._Save.jpg/200px-Narodna_biblioteka_i_Hram_Sv._Save.jpg" width="200" height="150" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Narodna_biblioteka_i_Hram_Sv._Save.jpg/300px-Narodna_biblioteka_i_Hram_Sv._Save.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Narodna_biblioteka_i_Hram_Sv._Save.jpg/400px-Narodna_biblioteka_i_Hram_Sv._Save.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4288" data-file-height="3216" /></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><a href="/wiki/National_Library_of_Serbia" title="National Library of Serbia">National Library of Serbia</a> in Belgrade</div>
</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Matica_Srpska_-_panoramio_(2).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Matica_Srpska_-_panoramio_%282%29.jpg/200px-Matica_Srpska_-_panoramio_%282%29.jpg" width="200" height="133" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Matica_Srpska_-_panoramio_%282%29.jpg/300px-Matica_Srpska_-_panoramio_%282%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Matica_Srpska_-_panoramio_%282%29.jpg/400px-Matica_Srpska_-_panoramio_%282%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1065" /></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><a href="/wiki/Matica_Srpska" class="mw-redirect" title="Matica Srpska">Matica Srpska</a> in <a href="/wiki/Novi_Sad" title="Novi Sad">Novi Sad</a></div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Serbia spent 0.64% of GDP on scientific research in 2012, which is one of the lowest R&amp;D budgets in Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-237" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-237">[237]</a></sup> Serbia has a long history of excellence in maths and computer sciences which has created a strong pool of engineering talent, although economic sanctions during the 1990s and chronic underinvestment in research forced many scientific professionals to leave the country.<sup id="cite_ref-238" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-238">[238]</a></sup> Nevertheless, there are several areas in which Serbia still excels such as growing information technology sector, which includes software development as well as outsourcing. It generated $200 million in exports in 2011, both from international investors and a significant number of dynamic homegrown enterprises.<sup id="cite_ref-239" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-239">[239]</a></sup> In 2005 the global technology giant, <a href="/wiki/Microsoft" title="Microsoft">Microsoft</a>, founded the Microsoft Development Center, only its fourth such centre in the world. Among the scientific institutes operating in Serbia, the largest are the <a href="/wiki/Mihajlo_Pupin_Institute" title="Mihajlo Pupin Institute">Mihajlo Pupin Institute</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vin%C4%8Da_Nuclear_Institute" title="Vinča Nuclear Institute">Vinča Nuclear Institute</a>, both in Belgrade. The <a href="/wiki/Serbian_Academy_of_Sciences_and_Arts" title="Serbian Academy of Sciences and Arts">Serbian Academy of Sciences and Arts</a> is a <a href="/wiki/Learned_society" title="Learned society">learned society</a> promoting science and arts from its inception in 1841.<sup id="cite_ref-240" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-240">[240]</a></sup> With a strong science and technological ecosystem, Serbia has produced a number of renowned scientists that have greatly contributed to the field of science and technology.</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Nikola_Tesla" title="Nikola Tesla">Nikola Tesla</a>, <a href="/wiki/Electrical_engineer" class="mw-redirect" title="Electrical engineer">electrical engineer</a> and inventor, best known for his contributions to the design of the modern <a href="/wiki/Alternating_current" title="Alternating current">alternating current</a> (AC) <a href="/wiki/Electricity_supply" class="mw-redirect" title="Electricity supply">electricity supply</a> system including the AC <a href="/wiki/Induction_motor" title="Induction motor">induction motor</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-241" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-241">[241]</a></sup> The <i><a href="/wiki/Tesla_(unit)" title="Tesla (unit)">tesla</a></i> is the SI derived unit of magnetic flux density and was named after Tesla.<sup id="cite_ref-242" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-242">[242]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Mihajlo_Idvorski_Pupin" class="mw-redirect" title="Mihajlo Idvorski Pupin">Mihajlo Pupin</a> discovered a means of greatly extending the range of long-distance telephone communication by placing loading coils of wire (known as Pupin coils) at predetermined intervals along the transmitting wire (known as "pupinization").<sup id="cite_ref-243" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-243">[243]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Milutin_Milankovi%C4%87" title="Milutin Milanković">Milutin Milanković</a> is known for his theory of ice ages, suggesting a relationship between the Earth's long-term climate changes and periodic changes in its orbit, now known as Milankovitch cycles.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Mihailo_Petrovi%C4%87" title="Mihailo Petrović">Mihailo Petrović</a> is known for having contributed significantly to differential equations and phenomenology, as well as inventing one of the first prototypes of an analog computer.</li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Serbian_culture" title="Serbian culture">Serbian culture</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cultural_Heritage_of_Serbia" title="Cultural Heritage of Serbia">Cultural Heritage of Serbia</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Archangel_Gabriel_Outside_Jesus%27_Tomb_after_Resurrection.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Archangel_Gabriel_Outside_Jesus%27_Tomb_after_Resurrection.png/150px-Archangel_Gabriel_Outside_Jesus%27_Tomb_after_Resurrection.png" width="150" height="207" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Archangel_Gabriel_Outside_Jesus%27_Tomb_after_Resurrection.png/225px-Archangel_Gabriel_Outside_Jesus%27_Tomb_after_Resurrection.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Archangel_Gabriel_Outside_Jesus%27_Tomb_after_Resurrection.png/300px-Archangel_Gabriel_Outside_Jesus%27_Tomb_after_Resurrection.png 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="885" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Archangel_Gabriel_Outside_Jesus%27_Tomb_after_Resurrection.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/White_Angel" title="White Angel">White Angel</a> (1235) fresco from Mileševa monastery. This fresco was sent as a message in the first <a href="/wiki/Satellite_television" title="Satellite television">satellite broadcast</a> signal from <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a> to <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">America</a> after the <a href="/wiki/Cuban_Missile_Crisis" title="Cuban Missile Crisis">Cuban Missile Crisis</a>, as a <a href="/wiki/Symbol" title="Symbol">symbol</a> of <a href="/wiki/Peace" title="Peace">peace</a> and <a href="/wiki/Civilization" title="Civilization">civilization</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-prijepolje_244-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-prijepolje-244">[244]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>For centuries straddling the boundaries between East and West, the territory of Serbia had been divided among the Eastern and <a href="/wiki/Western_Roman_Empire" title="Western Roman Empire">Western</a> halves of the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Roman Empire</a>; then between <a href="/wiki/Byzantium" title="Byzantium">Byzantium</a> and the Kingdom of Hungary; and in the Early modern period between the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Habsburg_Monarchy" title="Habsburg Monarchy">Habsburg Empire</a>. These overlapping influences have resulted in cultural varieties throughout Serbia; its north leans to the profile of Central Europe, while the south is characteristic of the wider Balkans and even the Mediterranean. The Byzantine influence on Serbia was profound, firstly through the introduction of <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Christianity" title="Eastern Christianity">Eastern Christianity</a> (Orthodoxy) in the Early Middle Ages. The Serbian Orthodox Church has had an enduring status in Serbia, with the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Serb_Orthodox_monasteries" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Serb Orthodox monasteries">many Serbian monasteries</a> constituting the most valuable cultural monuments left from <a href="/wiki/Serbia_in_the_Middle_Ages" title="Serbia in the Middle Ages">Serbia in the Middle Ages</a>. Serbia has seen influences of <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Venice" title="Republic of Venice">Republic of Venice</a> as well, mainly though trade, literature and <a href="/wiki/Romanesque_art" title="Romanesque art">romanesque architecture</a>.</p>
<p>Serbia has five cultural monuments inscribed in the list of <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">UNESCO World Heritage</a>: the early medieval capital <a href="/wiki/Stari_Ras" title="Stari Ras">Stari Ras</a> and the 13th-century monastery <a href="/wiki/Sopo%C4%87ani" title="Sopoćani">Sopoćani</a>; the 12th-century <a href="/wiki/Studenica_monastery" class="mw-redirect" title="Studenica monastery">Studenica monastery</a>; the Roman complex of <a href="/wiki/Gamzigrad" title="Gamzigrad">Gamzigrad–Felix Romuliana</a>; medieval tombstones <a href="/wiki/Ste%C4%87ci" class="mw-redirect" title="Stećci">Stećci</a>; and finally the endangered <a href="/wiki/Medieval_Monuments_in_Kosovo" title="Medieval Monuments in Kosovo">Medieval Monuments in Kosovo</a> (the monasteries of <a href="/wiki/Visoki_De%C4%8Dani" title="Visoki Dečani">Visoki Dečani</a>, <a href="/wiki/Our_Lady_of_Ljevi%C5%A1" title="Our Lady of Ljeviš">Our Lady of Ljeviš</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gra%C4%8Danica_Monastery" title="Gračanica Monastery">Gračanica</a> and <a href="/wiki/Patriarchal_Monastery_of_Pe%C4%87" class="mw-redirect" title="Patriarchal Monastery of Peć">Patriarchal Monastery of Peć</a>).</p>
<p>There are two literary monuments on UNESCO's <a href="/wiki/Memory_of_the_World_Programme" title="Memory of the World Programme">Memory of the World Programme</a>: the 12th-century <i><a href="/wiki/Miroslav_Gospel" title="Miroslav Gospel">Miroslav Gospel</a></i>, and scientist <a href="/wiki/Nikola_Tesla" title="Nikola Tesla">Nikola Tesla</a>'s valuable archive. The <i><a href="/wiki/Slava" title="Slava">slava</a></i> (patron saint veneration) is inscribed on <a href="/wiki/UNESCO_Intangible_Cultural_Heritage_Lists" title="UNESCO Intangible Cultural Heritage Lists">UNESCO Intangible Cultural Heritage Lists</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Minister_of_Culture_(Serbia)" class="mw-redirect" title="Minister of Culture (Serbia)">Ministry of Culture and Information</a> is tasked with preserving the nation's <a href="/wiki/Cultural_Heritage_of_Serbia" title="Cultural Heritage of Serbia">cultural heritage</a> and overseeing its development. Further activities supporting development of culture are undertaken at local government level.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Art_and_architecture">Art and architecture</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Serbian_art" title="Serbian art">Serbian art</a> and <a href="/wiki/Serbian_architecture" class="mw-redirect" title="Serbian architecture">Serbian architecture</a></div>
<p>Traces of Roman and early Byzantine Empire architectural heritage are found in many royal cities and palaces in Serbia, like <a href="/wiki/Sirmium" title="Sirmium">Sirmium</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gamzigrad" title="Gamzigrad">Felix Romuliana</a> and <a href="/wiki/Justiniana_Prima" title="Justiniana Prima">Justiniana Prima</a>.</p>
<p>Serbian monasteries are the pinnacle of Serbian medieval art. At the beginning, they were under the influence of <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Art" class="mw-redirect" title="Byzantine Art">Byzantine Art</a> which was particularly felt after the fall of Constantinople in 1204, when many Byzantine artists fled to Serbia. The most noted of these monasteries is <a href="/wiki/Studenica_monastery" class="mw-redirect" title="Studenica monastery">Studenica</a> (built around 1190). It was a model for later monasteries, like the <a href="/wiki/Mile%C5%A1eva" class="mw-redirect" title="Mileševa">Mileševa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sopo%C4%87ani" title="Sopoćani">Sopoćani</a>, <a href="/wiki/%C5%BDi%C4%8Da" title="Žiča">Žiča</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gra%C4%8Danica_monastery" class="mw-redirect" title="Gračanica monastery">Gračanica</a> and <a href="/wiki/Visoki_De%C4%8Dani" title="Visoki Dečani">Visoki Dečani</a>. In the end of 14th and the 15th centuries, autochotonous architectural style known as <a href="/wiki/Morava_architectural_school" title="Morava architectural school">Morava style</a> evolved in area around Morava Valley. A characteristic of this style was the wealthy decoration of the frontal church walls. Examples of this include <a href="/wiki/Manasija" title="Manasija">Manasija</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ravanica" title="Ravanica">Ravanica</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kaleni%C4%87_Monastery" class="mw-redirect" title="Kalenić Monastery">Kalenić</a> monasteries.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Kosovo_Maiden,_Uro%C5%A1_Predi%C4%87,_1919.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Kosovo_Maiden%2C_Uro%C5%A1_Predi%C4%87%2C_1919.jpg/300px-Kosovo_Maiden%2C_Uro%C5%A1_Predi%C4%87%2C_1919.jpg" width="300" height="215" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Kosovo_Maiden%2C_Uro%C5%A1_Predi%C4%87%2C_1919.jpg/450px-Kosovo_Maiden%2C_Uro%C5%A1_Predi%C4%87%2C_1919.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Kosovo_Maiden%2C_Uro%C5%A1_Predi%C4%87%2C_1919.jpg/600px-Kosovo_Maiden%2C_Uro%C5%A1_Predi%C4%87%2C_1919.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="734" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Kosovo_Maiden,_Uro%C5%A1_Predi%C4%87,_1919.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<i><a href="/wiki/Kosovo_Maiden" title="Kosovo Maiden">Kosovo Maiden</a></i> by <a href="/wiki/Uro%C5%A1_Predi%C4%87" title="Uroš Predić">Uroš Predić</a>, arguably the most famous Serbian painting, depicting a girl walking over Kosovo field after <a href="/wiki/Kosovo_Battle" class="mw-redirect" title="Kosovo Battle">Kosovo Battle</a> in 1389, and helping wounded warriors.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Icons and fresco paintings are often considered the peak of Serbian art. The most famous frescos are <a href="/wiki/White_Angel" title="White Angel">White Angel</a> (Mileševa monastery), <i>Crucifixion</i> (Studenica monastery) and <i>Dormition of the Virgin</i> (Sopoćani).</p>
<p>Country is dotted with many well-preserved medieval fortifications and castles such as <a href="/wiki/Smederevo_Fortress" title="Smederevo Fortress">Smederevo Fortress</a> (largest lowland fortress in Europe), <a href="/wiki/Golubac_Fortress" title="Golubac Fortress">Golubac</a>, <a href="/wiki/Magli%C4%8D" title="Maglič">Maglič</a>, <a href="/wiki/Soko_Grad_(Sokobanja)" title="Soko Grad (Sokobanja)">Soko grad</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ostrvica_Fortress" title="Ostrvica Fortress">Ostrvica</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ram_Fortress" title="Ram Fortress">Ram</a>.</p>
<p>During the time of Ottoman occupation, Serbian art was virtually non-existent, with the exception of several Serbian artists who lived in the lands ruled by the <a href="/wiki/Habsburg_Monarchy" title="Habsburg Monarchy">Habsburg Monarchy</a>. Traditional Serbian art showed some <a href="/wiki/Baroque" title="Baroque">Baroque</a> influences at the end of the 18th century as shown in the works of <a href="/wiki/Nikola_Ne%C5%A1kovi%C4%87" title="Nikola Nešković">Nikola Nešković</a>, <a href="/wiki/Teodor_Kra%C4%8Dun" title="Teodor Kračun">Teodor Kračun</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zaharije_Orfelin" title="Zaharije Orfelin">Zaharije Orfelin</a> and Jakov Orfelin.<sup id="cite_ref-245" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-245">[245]</a></sup></p>
<p>Serbian painting showed the influence of <a href="/wiki/Biedermeier" title="Biedermeier">Biedermeier</a>, <a href="/wiki/Neoclassicism" title="Neoclassicism">Neoclassicism</a> and Romanticism during the 19th century. The most important Serbian painters of the first half of the 20th century were <a href="/wiki/Paja_Jovanovi%C4%87" title="Paja Jovanović">Paja Jovanović</a> and <a href="/wiki/Uro%C5%A1_Predi%C4%87" title="Uroš Predić">Uroš Predić</a> of <a href="/wiki/Realism_(arts)" title="Realism (arts)">Realism</a>, Cubist <a href="/wiki/Sava_%C5%A0umanovi%C4%87" title="Sava Šumanović">Sava Šumanović</a>, <a href="/wiki/Milena_Pavlovi%C4%87-Barili" title="Milena Pavlović-Barili">Milena Pavlović-Barili</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nade%C5%BEda_Petrovi%C4%87" title="Nadežda Petrović">Nadežda Petrović</a> of Impressionism, Expressionist <a href="/wiki/Milan_Konjovi%C4%87" title="Milan Konjović">Milan Konjović</a>. Noted painters of the second half of 20th century include <a href="/wiki/Marko_%C4%8Celebonovi%C4%87" title="Marko Čelebonović">Marko Čelebonović</a>, <a href="/wiki/Petar_Lubarda" title="Petar Lubarda">Petar Lubarda</a>, <a href="/wiki/Milo_Milunovi%C4%87" title="Milo Milunović">Milo Milunović</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Veli%C4%8Dkovi%C4%87" title="Vladimir Veličković">Vladimir Veličković</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-246" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-246">[246]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Anastas_Jovanovi%C4%87" title="Anastas Jovanović">Anastas Jovanović</a> was one of the earliest photographes in the world, while <a href="/wiki/Marina_Abramovi%C4%87" title="Marina Abramović">Marina Abramović</a> is one of the world leading performance artists. <a href="/wiki/Pirot_carpet" title="Pirot carpet">Pirot carpet</a> is known as one of the most important traditional handicrafts in Serbia.</p>
<p>There are around 100 art museums in Serbia, of which the most prominent is the <a href="/wiki/National_Museum_of_Serbia" title="National Museum of Serbia">National Museum of Serbia</a>, founded in 1844; it houses one of the largest art collections in the Balkans with more than 400,000 exhibits, over 5,600 paintings and 8,400 drawings and prints, including many foreign masterpiece collections. Other art museums of note are <a href="/wiki/Museum_of_Contemporary_Art_(Belgrade)" class="mw-redirect" title="Museum of Contemporary Art (Belgrade)">Museum of Contemporary Art</a> in Belgrade and <a href="/wiki/Museum_of_Vojvodina" title="Museum of Vojvodina">Museum of Vojvodina</a> in Novi Sad.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Literature">Literature</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Serbian_literature" title="Serbian literature">Serbian literature</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Miroslav%27s_Gospel_001.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Miroslav%27s_Gospel_001.jpg/250px-Miroslav%27s_Gospel_001.jpg" width="250" height="167" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Miroslav%27s_Gospel_001.jpg/375px-Miroslav%27s_Gospel_001.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Miroslav%27s_Gospel_001.jpg/500px-Miroslav%27s_Gospel_001.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="2000" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Miroslav%27s_Gospel_001.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Miroslav%27s_Gospel" class="mw-redirect" title="Miroslav's Gospel">Miroslav's Gospel</a> (1186)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The beginning of Serbian literacy dates back to the activity of the brothers <a href="/wiki/Cyril_and_Methodius" class="mw-redirect" title="Cyril and Methodius">Cyril and Methodius</a> in the Balkans. Monuments of Serbian literacy from the early 11th century can be found, written in <a href="/wiki/Glagolitic" class="mw-redirect" title="Glagolitic">Glagolitic</a>. Starting in the 12th century, books were written in <a href="/wiki/Cyrillic" class="mw-redirect" title="Cyrillic">Cyrillic</a>. From this epoch, the oldest Serbian Cyrillic book editorial are the <a href="/wiki/Miroslav_Gospels" class="mw-redirect" title="Miroslav Gospels">Miroslav Gospels</a> from 1186. <i>The Miroslav Gospels</i> are considered to be the oldest book of Serbian medieval history and as such has entered <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Memory_of_the_World_Register" class="mw-redirect" title="Memory of the World Register">Memory of the World Register</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-mow_247-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mow-247">[247]</a></sup></p>
<p>Notable medieval authors include <a href="/wiki/Saint_Sava" title="Saint Sava">Saint Sava</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jefimija" title="Jefimija">Jefimija</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stefan_Lazarevi%C4%87" title="Stefan Lazarević">Stefan Lazarević</a>, <a href="/wiki/Constantine_of_Kostenets" title="Constantine of Kostenets">Constantine of Kostenets</a> and others.<sup id="cite_ref-248" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-248">[248]</a></sup> Due to Ottoman occupation, when every aspect of formal literacy stopped, Serbia stayed excluded from the entire <a href="/wiki/Renaissance" title="Renaissance">Renaissance</a> flow in Western culture. However, the tradition of oral story-telling blossomed, shaping itself through <a href="/wiki/Epic_poetry" title="Epic poetry">epic poetry</a> inspired by at the times still recent <a href="/wiki/Kosovo_battle" class="mw-redirect" title="Kosovo battle">Kosovo battle</a> and <a href="/wiki/Folklore" title="Folklore">folk tales</a> deeply rooted in <a href="/wiki/Slavic_mythology" class="mw-redirect" title="Slavic mythology">Slavic mythology</a>. <a href="/wiki/Serbian_epic_poetry" title="Serbian epic poetry">Serbian epic poetry</a> in those times has seen as the most effective way in preserving the national identity.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDragnich199429.E2.80.9330_249-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDragnich199429.E2.80.9330-249">[249]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-CaseNaimark2003_250-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CaseNaimark2003-250">[250]</a></sup> The oldest known, entirely fictional poems, gather around <i>Non-historic cycle</i>; this one is followed by poems inspired by events before, during and after Kosovo Battle. The special cycles are dedicated to Serbian legendary hero, <a href="/wiki/Marko_Kraljevi%C4%87" class="mw-disambig" title="Marko Kraljević">Marko Kraljević</a>, then about <a href="/wiki/Hajduk" title="Hajduk">hajduks</a> and <a href="/wiki/Uskok" class="mw-redirect" title="Uskok">uskoks</a>, and the last one dedicated to the liberation of Serbia in 19th century. Some of the best known folk ballads are <i>The Death of the Mother of the Jugović Family</i> and <a href="/wiki/Hasanaginica" title="Hasanaginica">The Mourning Song of the Noble Wife of the Asan Aga</a> (1646), translated into European languages by <a href="/wiki/Goethe" class="mw-redirect" title="Goethe">Goethe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Walter_Scott" title="Walter Scott">Walter Scott</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pushkin" class="mw-redirect" title="Pushkin">Pushkin</a> and <a href="/wiki/M%C3%A9rim%C3%A9e" class="mw-redirect" title="Mérimée">Mérimée</a>. The most notable tale from Serbian folklore is <a href="/wiki/The_Nine_Peahens_and_the_Golden_Apples" title="The Nine Peahens and the Golden Apples">The Nine Peahens and the Golden Apples</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-251" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-251">[251]</a></sup></p>
<p>Baroque trends in Serbian literature emerged in the late 17th century. Notable Baroque-influenced authors were <a href="/wiki/Gavril_Stefanovi%C4%87_Venclovi%C4%87" class="mw-redirect" title="Gavril Stefanović Venclović">Gavril Stefanović Venclović</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jovan_Raji%C4%87" title="Jovan Rajić">Jovan Rajić</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zaharije_Orfelin" title="Zaharije Orfelin">Zaharije Orfelin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Andrija_Zmajevi%C4%87" title="Andrija Zmajević">Andrija Zmajević</a> and others.<sup id="cite_ref-252" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-252">[252]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Dositej_Obradovi%C4%87" title="Dositej Obradović">Dositej Obradović</a> was the most prominent figure of the <a href="/wiki/Age_of_Enlightenment" title="Age of Enlightenment">Age of Enlightenment</a>, while the most notable <a href="/wiki/Classicism" title="Classicism">Classicist</a> writer was <a href="/wiki/Jovan_Sterija_Popovi%C4%87" title="Jovan Sterija Popović">Jovan Sterija Popović</a>, although his works also contained elements of Romanticism.<sup id="cite_ref-253" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-253">[253]</a></sup> In the era of national revival, in the first half of the 19th century, <a href="/wiki/Vuk_Stefanovi%C4%87_Karad%C5%BEi%C4%87" class="mw-redirect" title="Vuk Stefanović Karadžić">Vuk Stefanović Karadžić</a> collected Serbian <a href="/wiki/Folk_literature" class="mw-redirect" title="Folk literature">folk literature</a>, and reformed the Serbian language and spelling,<sup id="cite_ref-254" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-254">[254]</a></sup> paving the way for Serbian Romanticism. The first half of the 19th century was dominated by Romanticism, with <a href="/wiki/Branko_Radi%C4%8Devi%C4%87" title="Branko Radičević">Branko Radičević</a>, <a href="/wiki/%C4%90ura_Jak%C5%A1i%C4%87" title="Đura Jakšić">Đura Jakšić</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jovan_Jovanovi%C4%87_Zmaj" title="Jovan Jovanović Zmaj">Jovan Jovanović Zmaj</a> and <a href="/wiki/Laza_Kosti%C4%87" title="Laza Kostić">Laza Kostić</a> being the most notable representatives, while the second half of the century was marked by <a href="/wiki/Literary_realism" title="Literary realism">Realist</a> writers such as <a href="/wiki/Milovan_Gli%C5%A1i%C4%87" title="Milovan Glišić">Milovan Glišić</a>, <a href="/wiki/Laza_Lazarevi%C4%87" title="Laza Lazarević">Laza Lazarević</a>, <a href="/wiki/Simo_Matavulj" title="Simo Matavulj">Simo Matavulj</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stevan_Sremac" title="Stevan Sremac">Stevan Sremac</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vojislav_Ili%C4%87" title="Vojislav Ilić">Vojislav Ilić</a>, <a href="/wiki/Branislav_Nu%C5%A1i%C4%87" title="Branislav Nušić">Branislav Nušić</a>, <a href="/wiki/Radoje_Domanovi%C4%87" title="Radoje Domanović">Radoje Domanović</a> and <a href="/wiki/Borisav_Stankovi%C4%87" title="Borisav Stanković">Borisav Stanković</a>.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Stevan_Kragujevic,_Ivo_Andric_u_svom_domu.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Stevan_Kragujevic%2C_Ivo_Andric_u_svom_domu.JPG/220px-Stevan_Kragujevic%2C_Ivo_Andric_u_svom_domu.JPG" width="220" height="220" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Stevan_Kragujevic%2C_Ivo_Andric_u_svom_domu.JPG/330px-Stevan_Kragujevic%2C_Ivo_Andric_u_svom_domu.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Stevan_Kragujevic%2C_Ivo_Andric_u_svom_domu.JPG/440px-Stevan_Kragujevic%2C_Ivo_Andric_u_svom_domu.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2880" data-file-height="2880" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Stevan_Kragujevic,_Ivo_Andric_u_svom_domu.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Ivo_Andri%C4%87" title="Ivo Andrić">Ivo Andrić</a>, Serbian writer and the <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Literature" title="Nobel Prize in Literature">1961 winner of the Nobel Prize in Literature</a> in his home in <a href="/wiki/Belgrade" title="Belgrade">Belgrade</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The 20th century was dominated by the prose writers <a href="/wiki/Me%C5%A1a_Selimovi%C4%87" title="Meša Selimović">Meša Selimović</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Death_and_the_Dervish" title="Death and the Dervish">Death and the Dervish</a></i>), <a href="/wiki/Milo%C5%A1_Crnjanski" title="Miloš Crnjanski">Miloš Crnjanski</a> (<i>Migrations</i>), <a href="/wiki/Isidora_Sekuli%C4%87" title="Isidora Sekulić">Isidora Sekulić</a> (<i>The Cronicle of a Small Town Cemetery</i>), <a href="/wiki/Branko_%C4%86opi%C4%87" title="Branko Ćopić">Branko Ćopić</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Eagles_Fly_Early_(novel)" title="Eagles Fly Early (novel)">Eagles Fly Early</a></i>), <a href="/wiki/Borislav_Peki%C4%87" title="Borislav Pekić">Borislav Pekić</a> (<i>The Time of Miracles</i>), <a href="/wiki/Danilo_Ki%C5%A1" title="Danilo Kiš">Danilo Kiš</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/The_Encyclopedia_of_the_Dead" title="The Encyclopedia of the Dead">The Encyclopedia of the Dead</a></i>), <a href="/wiki/Dobrica_%C4%86osi%C4%87" title="Dobrica Ćosić">Dobrica Ćosić</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Koreni_(novel)" title="Koreni (novel)">The Roots</a></i>), <a href="/wiki/Aleksandar_Ti%C5%A1ma" title="Aleksandar Tišma">Aleksandar Tišma</a>, <a href="/wiki/Milorad_Pavi%C4%87" title="Milorad Pavić">Milorad Pavić</a> and others.<sup id="cite_ref-255" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-255">[255]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-256" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-256">[256]</a></sup> Pavić is the most widely acclaimed Serbian author of the beginning of the 21st century, most notably for his <i><a href="/wiki/Dictionary_of_the_Khazars" title="Dictionary of the Khazars">Dictionary of the Khazars</a></i> <i>(Хазарски речник/Hazarski rečnik)</i>, which has been translated into 24 languages. Notable poets include <a href="/wiki/Milan_Raki%C4%87" title="Milan Rakić">Milan Rakić</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jovan_Du%C4%8Di%C4%87" title="Jovan Dučić">Jovan Dučić</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vladislav_Petkovi%C4%87_Dis" title="Vladislav Petković Dis">Vladislav Petković Dis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rastko_Petrovi%C4%87" title="Rastko Petrović">Rastko Petrović</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stanislav_Vinaver" title="Stanislav Vinaver">Stanislav Vinaver</a>, <a href="/wiki/Du%C5%A1an_Mati%C4%87" title="Dušan Matić">Dušan Matić</a>, <a href="/wiki/Branko_Miljkovi%C4%87" title="Branko Miljković">Branko Miljković</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vasko_Popa" title="Vasko Popa">Vasko Popa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oskar_Davi%C4%8Do" title="Oskar Davičo">Oskar Davičo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Miodrag_Pavlovi%C4%87" title="Miodrag Pavlović">Miodrag Pavlović</a>, and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Stevan_Rai%C4%8Dkovi%C4%87&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Stevan Raičković (page does not exist)">Stevan Raičković</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-257" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-257">[257]</a></sup> Notable contemporary authors include <a href="/wiki/David_Albahari" title="David Albahari">David Albahari</a>, <a href="/wiki/Svetislav_Basara" title="Svetislav Basara">Svetislav Basara</a>, <a href="/wiki/Goran_Petrovi%C4%87" title="Goran Petrović">Goran Petrović</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gordana_Kui%C4%87" title="Gordana Kuić">Gordana Kuić</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vuk_Dra%C5%A1kovi%C4%87" title="Vuk Drašković">Vuk Drašković</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Vladislav_Bajac" title="Vladislav Bajac">Vladislav Bajac</a>.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Ivo_Andri%C4%87" title="Ivo Andrić">Ivo Andrić</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/The_Bridge_on_the_Drina" title="The Bridge on the Drina">The Bridge on the Drina</a></i>) is possibly the best-known Serbian author,;<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESnel2004209_258-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESnel2004209-258">[258]</a></sup> he was awarded the <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Literature" title="Nobel Prize in Literature">Nobel Prize in Literature</a> in 1961. The most beloved face of Serbian literature was <a href="/wiki/Desanka_Maksimovi%C4%87" title="Desanka Maksimović">Desanka Maksimović</a>, who for seven decades remained <i>the leading lady of Yugoslav poetry</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDeliso2009110_259-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDeliso2009110-259">[259]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVidan2016494_260-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVidan2016494-260">[260]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHawkesworth200015_261-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHawkesworth200015-261">[261]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHawkesworth2000203_262-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHawkesworth2000203-262">[262]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJuraga2002204_263-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJuraga2002204-263">[263]</a></sup> She is honored with statues, and postage stamps, and streets are named for her.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELuci.C4.8722_August_2007_264-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELuci.C4.8722_August_2007-264">[264]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTE.C5.A0uberKaramani.C4.872012327.E2.80.93328_265-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTE.C5.A0uberKaramani.C4.872012327.E2.80.93328-265">[265]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELuci.C4.8722_August_2007_264-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELuci.C4.8722_August_2007-264">[264]</a></sup> <sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHaag2002124_266-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHaag2002124-266">[266]</a></sup></p>
<p>There are 551 public libraries biggest of which are: <a href="/wiki/National_Library_of_Serbia" title="National Library of Serbia">National Library of Serbia</a> in Belgrade with funds of about 5 million volumes, and <a href="/wiki/Matica_Srpska" class="mw-redirect" title="Matica Srpska">Matica Srpska</a> (oldest Serbian cultural institution, founded in 1826) in Novi Sad with nearly 3.5 million volumes.<sup id="cite_ref-267" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-267">[267]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-268" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-268">[268]</a></sup> In 2010, there were 10,989 books and brochures published.<sup id="cite_ref-pod2.stat.gov.rs_100-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pod2.stat.gov.rs-100">[100]</a></sup> The book publishing market is dominated by several major publishers such as Laguna and Vulkan (both of which operate their own bookstore chains) and the industry's centerpiece event, annual <a href="/wiki/Belgrade_Book_Fair" title="Belgrade Book Fair">Belgrade Book Fair</a>, is the most visited cultural event in Serbia with 158,128 visitors in 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-269" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-269">[269]</a></sup> The highlight of the literary scene is awarding of <a href="/wiki/NIN_Prize" class="mw-redirect" title="NIN Prize">NIN Prize</a>, given every January since 1954 for the best newly published novel in Serbian language (during times of Yugoslavia, in Serbo-Croatian language).<sup id="cite_ref-270" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-270">[270]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Serbia" title="Music of Serbia">Music of Serbia</a></div>
<p>Composer and <a href="/wiki/Musicology" title="Musicology">musicologist</a> <a href="/wiki/Stevan_Stojanovi%C4%87_Mokranjac" class="mw-redirect" title="Stevan Stojanović Mokranjac">Stevan Stojanović Mokranjac</a> is considered the founder of modern Serbian music.<sup id="cite_ref-271" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-271">[271]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-272" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-272">[272]</a></sup> The Serbian composers of the first generation <a href="/wiki/Petar_Konjovi%C4%87" title="Petar Konjović">Petar Konjović</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stevan_Hristi%C4%87" title="Stevan Hristić">Stevan Hristić</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Miloje_Milojevi%C4%87" title="Miloje Milojević">Miloje Milojević</a> maintained the national expression and modernized the romanticism into the direction of impressionism. Other famous <a href="/wiki/European_classical_music" class="mw-redirect" title="European classical music">classical</a> Serbian composers include <a href="/wiki/Isidor_Baji%C4%87" title="Isidor Bajić">Isidor Bajić</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stanislav_Bini%C4%8Dki" title="Stanislav Binički">Stanislav Binički</a> and <a href="/wiki/Josif_Marinkovi%C4%87" title="Josif Marinković">Josif Marinković</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-273" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-273">[273]</a></sup> There are three opera houses in Serbia: <a href="/wiki/National_Theatre_in_Belgrade" title="National Theatre in Belgrade">Opera of the National Theatre</a> and <a href="/wiki/Madlenianum_Opera_and_Theatre" title="Madlenianum Opera and Theatre">Madlenianum Opera</a>, both in Belgrade, and <a href="/wiki/Serbian_National_Theatre" title="Serbian National Theatre">Opera of the Serbian National Theatre</a> in Novi Sad. Four symphonic orchestra operate in the country: <a href="/wiki/Belgrade_Philharmonic_Orchestra" title="Belgrade Philharmonic Orchestra">Belgrade Philharmonic Orchestra</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ni%C5%A1_Symphony_Orchestra" title="Niš Symphony Orchestra">Niš Symphony Orchestra</a>, Symphonic Orchestra of Radio Television of Serbia, and Novi Sad Philharmonic Orchestra. The Choir of Radio Television of Serbia is a leading vocal ensemble in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-274" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-274">[274]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Belgrade_Music_Festival" title="Belgrade Music Festival">BEMUS</a> is one of the most prominent classical music festivals in the South East Europe.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Filip_Visnjic_guslar.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Filip_Visnjic_guslar.jpg/170px-Filip_Visnjic_guslar.jpg" width="170" height="266" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Filip_Visnjic_guslar.jpg/255px-Filip_Visnjic_guslar.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Filip_Visnjic_guslar.jpg/340px-Filip_Visnjic_guslar.jpg 2x" data-file-width="344" data-file-height="539" /></a>

<a href="/wiki/Filip_Vi%C5%A1nji%C4%87" title="Filip Višnjić">Filip Višnjić</a> sings to the <a href="/wiki/Gusle" title="Gusle">gusle</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Traditional Serbian music includes various kinds of <a href="/wiki/Bagpipes" title="Bagpipes">bagpipes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Flutes" class="mw-redirect" title="Flutes">flutes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Blowing_horn" title="Blowing horn">horns</a>, <a href="/wiki/Trumpet" title="Trumpet">trumpets</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lutes" class="mw-redirect" title="Lutes">lutes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Psalteries" class="mw-redirect" title="Psalteries">psalteries</a>, drums and cymbals. The <i><a href="/wiki/Kolo_(dance)" title="Kolo (dance)">kolo</a></i> is the traditional collective folk dance, which has <a href="/wiki/Serbian_dances" title="Serbian dances">a number of varieties</a> throughout the regions. The most popular are those from <a href="/wiki/U%C5%BEice" title="Užice">Užice</a> and Morava region. <a href="/wiki/Serbian_epic_poetry" title="Serbian epic poetry">Sung epic poetry</a> has been an integral part of Serbian and Balkan music for centuries. In the highlands of Serbia these long poems are typically accompanied on a one-string fiddle called the <i><a href="/wiki/Gusle" title="Gusle">gusle</a></i>, and concern themselves with themes from history and mythology. There are records of <i>gusle</i> being played at the court of the 13th-century King <a href="/wiki/Stefan_Nemanji%C4%87" class="mw-redirect" title="Stefan Nemanjić">Stefan Nemanjić</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-275" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-275">[275]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Serbian_rock" class="mw-redirect" title="Serbian rock">Serbian rock</a> which was during the 1960s, 1970s and 1980s part of <a href="/wiki/SFR_Yugoslav_pop_and_rock_scene" class="mw-redirect" title="SFR Yugoslav pop and rock scene">former Yugoslav rock scene</a>, used to be well developed, featuring various rock genres, and was well covered in the media, which included numerous magazines, radio and TV shows. During the 1990s and 2000s popularity of rock music declined in Serbia, and although several major mainstream acts managed to sustain their popularity, an <a href="/wiki/Underground_music" title="Underground music">underground</a> and <a href="/wiki/Independent_music" title="Independent music">independent music</a> scene developed. The most notable Serbian rock acts include <a href="/wiki/Bajaga_i_Instruktori" title="Bajaga i Instruktori">Bajaga i Instruktori</a>, <a href="/wiki/%C4%90or%C4%91e_Bala%C5%A1evi%C4%87" title="Đorđe Balašević">Đorđe Balašević</a>, <a href="/wiki/Disciplina_Ki%C4%8Dme" class="mw-redirect" title="Disciplina Kičme">Disciplina Kičme</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ekatarina_Velika" title="Ekatarina Velika">Ekatarina Velika</a>, <a href="/wiki/Elektri%C4%8Dni_Orgazam" title="Električni Orgazam">Električni Orgazam</a>, <a href="/wiki/Galija" title="Galija">Galija</a>, <a href="/wiki/Idoli" title="Idoli">Idoli</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kerber" title="Kerber">Kerber</a>, <a href="/wiki/Korni_Grupa" title="Korni Grupa">Korni Grupa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Partibrejkers" title="Partibrejkers">Partibrejkers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pekin%C5%A1ka_Patka" title="Pekinška Patka">Pekinška Patka</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pop_Ma%C5%A1ina" title="Pop Mašina">Pop Mašina</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rambo_Amadeus" title="Rambo Amadeus">Rambo Amadeus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Riblja_%C4%8Corba" title="Riblja Čorba">Riblja Čorba</a>, <a href="/wiki/Smak" title="Smak">Smak</a>, <a href="/wiki/S_Vremena_Na_Vreme" title="S Vremena Na Vreme">S Vremena Na Vreme</a>, <a href="/wiki/%C5%A0arlo_Akrobata" title="Šarlo Akrobata">Šarlo Akrobata</a>, <a href="/wiki/Van_Gogh_(band)" title="Van Gogh (band)">Van Gogh</a>, <a href="/wiki/YU_Grupa" title="YU Grupa">YU Grupa</a>, and others.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:ESC_2007_Serbia_-_Marija_Serifovic_-_Molitva.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/ESC_2007_Serbia_-_Marija_Serifovic_-_Molitva.jpg/220px-ESC_2007_Serbia_-_Marija_Serifovic_-_Molitva.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/ESC_2007_Serbia_-_Marija_Serifovic_-_Molitva.jpg/330px-ESC_2007_Serbia_-_Marija_Serifovic_-_Molitva.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/ESC_2007_Serbia_-_Marija_Serifovic_-_Molitva.jpg/440px-ESC_2007_Serbia_-_Marija_Serifovic_-_Molitva.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1500" data-file-height="1000" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:ESC_2007_Serbia_-_Marija_Serifovic_-_Molitva.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Serbia won <a href="/wiki/Eurovision_Song_Contest_2007" title="Eurovision Song Contest 2007">Eurovision Song Contest 2007</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Serbian_pop" title="Serbian pop">Pop music</a> has mainstream popularity. <a href="/wiki/%C5%BDeljko_Joksimovi%C4%87" title="Željko Joksimović">Željko Joksimović</a> won second place at the <a href="/wiki/2004_Eurovision_Song_Contest" class="mw-redirect" title="2004 Eurovision Song Contest">2004 Eurovision Song Contest</a> and <a href="/wiki/Marija_%C5%A0erifovi%C4%87" title="Marija Šerifović">Marija Šerifović</a> managed to win the <a href="/wiki/2007_Eurovision_Song_Contest" class="mw-redirect" title="2007 Eurovision Song Contest">2007 Eurovision Song Contest</a> with the song "<a href="/wiki/Molitva" title="Molitva">Molitva</a>", and Serbia was the host of the <a href="/wiki/2008_Eurovision_Song_Contest" class="mw-redirect" title="2008 Eurovision Song Contest">2008 edition</a> of the contest. Most popular pop singers include likes of <a href="/wiki/Zdravko_%C4%8Coli%C4%87" title="Zdravko Čolić">Zdravko Čolić</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vlado_Georgiev" title="Vlado Georgiev">Vlado Georgiev</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nata%C5%A1a_Bekvalac" title="Nataša Bekvalac">Nataša Bekvalac</a> among others.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Turbo-folk" title="Turbo-folk">Turbo-folk</a> music is subgenre that has developed in Serbia in the late 1980s and the beginning of the 1990s and has since enjoyed an immense popularity. It is a blend of <a href="/wiki/Folk_music" title="Folk music">folk music</a> with <a href="/wiki/Pop_music" title="Pop music">pop</a> and/or <a href="/wiki/Dance_music" title="Dance music">dance</a> elements and can be seen as a result of the urbanization of folk music. In recent period turbo-folk featured even more pop music elements, and some of the performers were labeled as pop-folk. The most famous among them are <a href="/wiki/Svetlana_Ra%C5%BEnatovi%C4%87" class="mw-redirect" title="Svetlana Ražnatović">Ceca</a> (often considered to be the biggest music star of Serbia), <a href="/wiki/Jelena_Karleu%C5%A1a" title="Jelena Karleuša">Jelena Karleuša</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aca_Lukas" title="Aca Lukas">Aca Lukas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Seka_Aleksi%C4%87" title="Seka Aleksić">Seka Aleksić</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dragana_Mirkovi%C4%87" title="Dragana Mirković">Dragana Mirković</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dara_Bubamara" title="Dara Bubamara">Dara Bubamara</a>, <a href="/wiki/Indira_Radi%C4%87" title="Indira Radić">Indira Radić</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lepa_Brena" title="Lepa Brena">Lepa Brena</a>, arguably the most prominent performer of former <a href="/wiki/Yugoslavia" title="Yugoslavia">Yugoslavia</a>.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Balkan_Brass_Band" class="mw-redirect" title="Balkan Brass Band">Balkan Brass</a>, or <i>truba</i> ("trumpet") is a popular genre, especially in Central and Southern Serbia where Balkan Brass originated. The music has its tradition from the <a href="/wiki/First_Serbian_Uprising" title="First Serbian Uprising">First Serbian Uprising</a>. The trumpet was used as a military instrument to wake and gather soldiers and announce battles, the trumpet took on the role of entertainment during downtime, as soldiers used it to transpose popular folk songs. When the war ended and the soldiers returned to the rural life, the music entered civilian life and eventually became a music style, accompanying births, baptisms, weddings, and funerals. There are two main varieties of this genre, one from Western Serbia and the other from Southern Serbia. The best known Serbian Brass musician is <a href="/wiki/Boban_Markovi%C4%87" title="Boban Marković">Boban Marković</a>, also one of the biggest names in the world of modern brass band bandleaders.</p>
<p>Most popular music festival are <a href="/wiki/Gu%C4%8Da_Trumpet_Festival" title="Guča Trumpet Festival">Guča Trumpet Festival</a> with over 300,000 annual visitors and <a href="/wiki/Exit_(festival)" title="Exit (festival)">EXIT</a> in Novi Sad ("The best European festival" in 2007 by UK Festival Awards and Yourope – the European Association of the 40 largest festivals in Europe) with 200,000 visitors in 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-276" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-276">[276]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-277" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-277">[277]</a></sup> Other festivals include <a href="/wiki/Ni%C5%A1ville" title="Nišville">Nišville Jazz Festival</a> in Niš and <a href="/wiki/Gitarijada" title="Gitarijada">Gitarijada</a> rock festival in Zaječar.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Theatre_and_cinema">Theatre and cinema</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_Serbia" title="Cinema of Serbia">Cinema of Serbia</a></div>
<p>Serbia has a well-established theatrical tradition with <a href="/wiki/Joakim_Vuji%C4%87" title="Joakim Vujić">Joakim Vujić</a> considered the founder of modern Serbian theater.<sup id="cite_ref-Joakim_278-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Joakim-278">[278]</a></sup> Serbia has 38 professional theatres, the most important of which are <a href="/wiki/National_Theatre_in_Belgrade" title="National Theatre in Belgrade">National Theatre</a> in Belgrade, <a href="/wiki/Serbian_National_Theatre" title="Serbian National Theatre">Serbian National Theatre</a> in Novi Sad, <a href="/wiki/National_Theatre_in_Subotica" title="National Theatre in Subotica">National Theatre in Subotica</a>, <a href="/wiki/National_Theatre_in_Ni%C5%A1" title="National Theatre in Niš">National Theatre in Niš</a> and <a href="/wiki/Knja%C5%BEevsko-srpski_teatar" title="Knjaževsko-srpski teatar">Knjaževsko-srpski teatar</a> in Kragujevac (the oldest theatre in Serbia, established in 1835). The <a href="/wiki/Bitef" class="mw-redirect" title="Bitef">Belgrade International Theatre Festival – BITEF</a>, founded in 1967, is one of the oldest theater festivals in the world, and it has become one of the five biggest European festivals.<sup id="cite_ref-279" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-279">[279]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Sterijino_pozorje" title="Sterijino pozorje">Sterijino pozorje</a> is, on the other hand, festival showcasing national drama plays. The most important Serbian playwrighters were <a href="/wiki/Jovan_Sterija_Popovi%C4%87" title="Jovan Sterija Popović">Jovan Sterija Popović</a> and <a href="/wiki/Branislav_Nu%C5%A1i%C4%87" title="Branislav Nušić">Branislav Nušić</a>, while today renowned names are <a href="/wiki/Du%C5%A1an_Kova%C4%8Devi%C4%87" title="Dušan Kovačević">Dušan Kovačević</a> and <a href="/wiki/Biljana_Srbljanovi%C4%87" title="Biljana Srbljanović">Biljana Srbljanović</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-280" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-280">[280]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:177px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Emir_Kusturica_at_Guadalajara_film_festival_2009.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Emir_Kusturica_at_Guadalajara_film_festival_2009.jpg/175px-Emir_Kusturica_at_Guadalajara_film_festival_2009.jpg" width="175" height="261" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Emir_Kusturica_at_Guadalajara_film_festival_2009.jpg/263px-Emir_Kusturica_at_Guadalajara_film_festival_2009.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Emir_Kusturica_at_Guadalajara_film_festival_2009.jpg/350px-Emir_Kusturica_at_Guadalajara_film_festival_2009.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="3872" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Emir_Kusturica_at_Guadalajara_film_festival_2009.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Emir_Kusturica" title="Emir Kusturica">Emir Kusturica</a>, most famous Serbian film director, won the <a href="/wiki/Palme_d%27Or" title="Palme d'Or">Palme d'Or</a> twice at <a href="/wiki/Cannes_Film_Festival" title="Cannes Film Festival">Cannes Film Festival</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Serbian_cinema" class="mw-redirect" title="Serbian cinema">Serbian cinema</a> is one of the most dynamic smaller European cinematographies. Serbia's film industry is heavily subsidised by the government, mainly through grants approved by the Film Centre of Serbia. In 2011, there were 17 domestic feature films produced.<sup id="cite_ref-281" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-281">[281]</a></sup> There are 20 operating cinemas in the country, of which 10 are <a href="/wiki/Multiplex_(movie_theater)" title="Multiplex (movie theater)">multiplexes</a>, with total attendance exceeding 2.6 million and comparatively high percentage of 32.3% of total sold tickets for domestic films.<sup id="cite_ref-282" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-282">[282]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-283" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-283">[283]</a></sup> Modern <a href="/wiki/Pink_International_Company" title="Pink International Company">PFI Studios</a> located in <a href="/wiki/%C5%A0imanovci" title="Šimanovci">Šimanovci</a> is nowadays Serbia's only film studio complex; it consists of 9 state-of-the-art sound stages and attracts mainly international productions, primarily American and West European.<sup id="cite_ref-284" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-284">[284]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Yugoslav_Film_Archive" title="Yugoslav Film Archive">Yugoslav Film Archive</a> used to be former Yugoslavia's and now is Serbia national film archive – with over 95 thousand film prints, it is among five largest film archives in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-285" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-285">[285]</a></sup></p>
<p>Serbian cinema dates back to 1896 with the release of the oldest movie in the Balkans, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Life_and_Deeds_of_the_Immortal_Vo%C5%BEd_Kara%C4%91or%C4%91e" title="The Life and Deeds of the Immortal Vožd Karađorđe">The Life and Deeds of the Immortal Vožd Karađorđe</a></i>, a biography about Serbian revolutionary leader, <a href="/wiki/Kara%C4%91or%C4%91e" title="Karađorđe">Karađorđe</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-286" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-286">[286]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-287" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-287">[287]</a></sup></p>
<p>The most famous Serbian filmmaker is <a href="/wiki/Emir_Kusturica" title="Emir Kusturica">Emir Kusturica</a> who won two <a href="/wiki/Golden_Palm" class="mw-redirect" title="Golden Palm">Golden Palms</a> for Best Feature Film at the <a href="/wiki/Cannes_Film_Festival" title="Cannes Film Festival">Cannes Film Festival</a>, for <i><a href="/wiki/When_Father_Was_Away_on_Business" title="When Father Was Away on Business">When Father Was Away on Business</a></i> in 1985 and then again for <i><a href="/wiki/Underground_(1995_film)" title="Underground (1995 film)">Underground</a></i> in 1995.<sup id="cite_ref-288" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-288">[288]</a></sup> Other renowned directors include <a href="/wiki/Goran_Paskaljevi%C4%87" title="Goran Paskaljević">Goran Paskaljević</a>, <a href="/wiki/Du%C5%A1an_Makavejev" title="Dušan Makavejev">Dušan Makavejev</a>, <a href="/wiki/Goran_Markovi%C4%87_(film_director)" class="mw-redirect" title="Goran Marković (film director)">Goran Marković</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sr%C4%91an_Dragojevi%C4%87" title="Srđan Dragojević">Srđan Dragojević</a> and <a href="/wiki/Srdan_Golubovi%C4%87" title="Srdan Golubović">Srdan Golubović</a> among others. <a href="/wiki/Steve_Tesich" title="Steve Tesich">Steve Tesich</a>, Serbian-American screenwriter, won the <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="Academy Award">Academy Award</a> for <a href="/wiki/Best_Original_Screenplay" class="mw-redirect" title="Best Original Screenplay">Best Original Screenplay</a> in 1979 for the movie <a href="/wiki/Breaking_Away" title="Breaking Away">Breaking Away</a>.</p>
<p>Some of the most prominent movie stars in Serbia have left celebrated heritage in cinematography of Yugoslavia as well. Notable mentions are <a href="/wiki/Zoran_Radmilovi%C4%87" title="Zoran Radmilović">Zoran Radmilović</a>, <a href="/wiki/Radmila_Savi%C4%87evi%C4%87" title="Radmila Savićević">Radmila Savićević</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pavle_Vuisi%C4%87" title="Pavle Vuisić">Pavle Vuisić</a>, <a href="/wiki/Olivera_Markovi%C4%87" title="Olivera Marković">Olivera Marković</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mija_Aleksi%C4%87" title="Mija Aleksić">Mija Aleksić</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ru%C5%BEica_Soki%C4%87" title="Ružica Sokić">Ružica Sokić</a>, <a href="/wiki/Miodrag_Petrovi%C4%87_%C4%8Ckalja" class="mw-redirect" title="Miodrag Petrović Čkalja">Miodrag Petrović Čkalja</a>, <a href="/wiki/Seka_Sabli%C4%87" title="Seka Sablić">Seka Sablić</a>, <a href="/wiki/Velimir_Bata_%C5%BDivojinovi%C4%87" class="mw-redirect" title="Velimir Bata Živojinović">Velimir Bata Živojinović</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mira_Banjac" title="Mira Banjac">Mira Banjac</a>, <a href="/wiki/Danilo_Bata_Stojkovi%C4%87" class="mw-redirect" title="Danilo Bata Stojković">Danilo Bata Stojković</a>, <a href="/wiki/Olivera_Katarina" title="Olivera Katarina">Olivera Katarina</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dragan_Nikoli%C4%87" title="Dragan Nikolić">Dragan Nikolić</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mira_Stupica" title="Mira Stupica">Mira Stupica</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nikola_Simi%C4%87" class="mw-disambig" title="Nikola Simić">Nikola Simić</a>, <a href="/wiki/Svetlana_Bojkovi%C4%87" title="Svetlana Bojković">Svetlana Bojković</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ljubi%C5%A1a_Samard%C5%BEi%C4%87" title="Ljubiša Samardžić">Ljubiša Samardžić</a>, <a href="/wiki/Neda_Arneri%C4%87" title="Neda Arnerić">Neda Arnerić</a>, <a href="/wiki/Petar_Kralj" title="Petar Kralj">Petar Kralj</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tanja_Bo%C5%A1kovi%C4%87" title="Tanja Bošković">Tanja Bošković</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aleksandar_Ber%C4%8Dek" title="Aleksandar Berček">Aleksandar Berček</a>, <a href="/wiki/Radmila_%C5%BDivkovi%C4%87" title="Radmila Živković">Radmila Živković</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bora_Todorovi%C4%87" title="Bora Todorović">Bora Todorović</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mirjana_Karanovi%C4%87" title="Mirjana Karanović">Mirjana Karanović</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stevo_%C5%BDigon" title="Stevo Žigon">Stevo Žigon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ljiljana_Blagojevi%C4%87" title="Ljiljana Blagojević">Ljiljana Blagojević</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vlastimir_%C4%90uza_Stojiljkovi%C4%87" title="Vlastimir Đuza Stojiljković">Vlastimir Đuza Stojiljković</a> and others. Some names of newer generation are <a href="/wiki/Vesna_Trivali%C4%87" title="Vesna Trivalić">Vesna Trivalić</a>, <a href="/wiki/Neboj%C5%A1a_Glogovac" title="Nebojša Glogovac">Nebojša Glogovac</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dubravka_Mijatovi%C4%87" title="Dubravka Mijatović">Dubravka Mijatović</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nata%C5%A1a_Ninkovi%C4%87" title="Nataša Ninković">Nataša Ninković</a>.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Milena_Dravi%C4%87" title="Milena Dravić">Milena Dravić</a> is the most celebrated actress in Serbian and Yugoslavian cinematography. The actress has won <a href="/wiki/Cannes_Film_Festival_Award_for_Best_Actress" title="Cannes Film Festival Award for Best Actress">Best Actress Award</a> on <a href="/wiki/Cannes_Film_Festival" title="Cannes Film Festival">Cannes Film Festival</a> in 1980 and 10 <a href="/wiki/Pula_Film_Festival" title="Pula Film Festival">Golden Arena</a> awards (Yugoslav equivalent for Academy Award).</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Media_of_Serbia" title="Media of Serbia">Media of Serbia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Media_freedom_in_Serbia" title="Media freedom in Serbia">Media freedom in Serbia</a></div>
<p>The freedom of the press and the freedom of speech are guaranteed by the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Serbia" title="Constitution of Serbia">constitution of Serbia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-289" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-289">[289]</a></sup> Serbia is ranked 54th out of 180 countries in the 2014 <a href="/wiki/Press_Freedom_Index" title="Press Freedom Index">Press Freedom Index</a> report compiled by <a href="/wiki/Reporters_Without_Borders" title="Reporters Without Borders">Reporters Without Borders</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-290" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-290">[290]</a></sup> Both reports noted that media outlets and journalists continue to face partisan and government pressure over editorial policies. Also, the media are now more heavily dependent on advertising contracts and government subsidies to survive financially.<sup id="cite_ref-291" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-291">[291]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Avala_Tower.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Avala_Tower.jpg/170px-Avala_Tower.jpg" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Avala_Tower.jpg/255px-Avala_Tower.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Avala_Tower.jpg/340px-Avala_Tower.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1500" data-file-height="2000" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Avala_Tower.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Avala_Tower" title="Avala Tower">Avala Tower</a>, the tallest tower in the Balkans</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>According to AGB Nielsen Research in 2009, Serbs on average watch five hours of television per day, making it the highest average in Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-292" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-292">[292]</a></sup> There are seven nationwide <a href="/wiki/Free-to-air" title="Free-to-air">free-to-air</a> television channels, with public broadcaster <a href="/wiki/Radio_Television_of_Serbia" title="Radio Television of Serbia">Radio Television of Serbia (RTS)</a> operating three (<a href="/wiki/RTS1" title="RTS1">RTS1</a>, <a href="/wiki/RTS2" title="RTS2">RTS2</a> and RTS3) and remaining four are private broadcasters: <a href="/wiki/Prva_Srpska_Televizija" title="Prva Srpska Televizija">Prva</a>, <a href="/wiki/B92" title="B92">B92</a>, <a href="/wiki/RTV_Pink" title="RTV Pink">Pink</a> and <a href="/wiki/Happy_TV" title="Happy TV">Happy TV</a>. Viewing shares for these channels in 2012 were as follows: 23.5% for RTS1, 19.6% for Pink, 16.1% for Prva, 8.1% for B92, 3.6% for RTS2, and 2.8% for Happy TV.<sup id="cite_ref-293" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-293">[293]</a></sup> There are 28 regional television channels and 74 local television channels.<sup id="cite_ref-pod2.stat.gov.rs_100-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pod2.stat.gov.rs-100">[100]</a></sup> Besides terrestrial channels there are dozens Serbian television channels available only on cable or satellite.</p>
<p>There are 220 radio stations in Serbia.<sup id="cite_ref-pod2.stat.gov.rs_100-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pod2.stat.gov.rs-100">[100]</a></sup> Out of these, seven are radio stations with national coverage, including three of public broadcaster <a href="/wiki/Radio_Television_of_Serbia" title="Radio Television of Serbia">Radio Television of Serbia</a> (<a href="/wiki/Radio_Belgrade" title="Radio Belgrade">Radio Belgrade 1</a>, <a href="/wiki/Radio_Belgrade" title="Radio Belgrade">Radio Belgrade 2/Radio Belgrade 3</a> and Radio Belgrade 202), and four private ones (Radio S1, Radio S2, Play Radio, and Radio Hit FM). Also, there are 49 regional stations and 162 local stations.<sup id="cite_ref-294" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-294">[294]</a></sup></p>
<p>There are 340 <a href="/wiki/Newspapers" class="mw-redirect" title="Newspapers">newspapers</a> published in Serbia<sup id="cite_ref-pod2.stat.gov.rs_100-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pod2.stat.gov.rs-100">[100]</a></sup> of which 12 are daily newspapers. Dailies <i><a href="/wiki/Politika" title="Politika">Politika</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Danas_(newspaper)" title="Danas (newspaper)">Danas</a></i> are Serbia's <a href="/wiki/Papers_of_record" class="mw-redirect" title="Papers of record">papers of record</a>, former being the oldest newspaper in the Balkans, founded in 1904.<sup id="cite_ref-295" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-295">[295]</a></sup> Highest circulation newspapers are tabloids <i><a href="/wiki/Ve%C4%8Dernje_Novosti" class="mw-redirect" title="Večernje Novosti">Večernje Novosti</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Blic" title="Blic">Blic</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Kurir" title="Kurir">Kurir</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Informer_(newspaper)" title="Informer (newspaper)">Informer</a></i>, all with more than 100,000 copies sold.<sup id="cite_ref-296" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-296">[296]</a></sup> There are one daily newspaper devoted to sports – <i><a href="/wiki/Sportski_%C5%BEurnal" title="Sportski žurnal">Sportski žurnal</a></i>, one business daily <i>Privredni pregled</i>, two regional newspapers (<i><a href="/wiki/Dnevnik_(Serbia)" class="mw-redirect" title="Dnevnik (Serbia)">Dnevnik</a></i> published in Novi Sad and <i>Narodne novine</i> from Niš), and one minority-language daily (<i><a href="/wiki/Magyar_Szo" class="mw-redirect" title="Magyar Szo">Magyar Szo</a></i> in Hungarian, published in Subotica).</p>
<p>There are 1,262 <a href="/wiki/Magazines" class="mw-redirect" title="Magazines">magazines</a> published in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-pod2.stat.gov.rs_100-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pod2.stat.gov.rs-100">[100]</a></sup> Those include weekly <a href="/wiki/News_magazine" title="News magazine">news magazines</a> <i><a href="/wiki/NIN_(magazine)" title="NIN (magazine)">NIN</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Vreme" title="Vreme">Vreme</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Nedeljnik" title="Nedeljnik">Nedeljnik</a></i>, popular science magazine of <i><a href="/wiki/Politikin_Zabavnik" title="Politikin Zabavnik">Politikin Zabavnik</a></i>, women's <i><a href="/wiki/Lepota_%26_Zdravlje" title="Lepota &amp; Zdravlje">Lepota &amp; Zdravlje</a></i>, auto magazine <i>SAT revija</i>, IT magazine <i><a href="/wiki/Svet_kompjutera" title="Svet kompjutera">Svet kompjutera</a></i>. In addition, there is a wide selection of Serbian editions of international magazines, such as <i><a href="/wiki/Cosmopolitan_(magazine)" title="Cosmopolitan (magazine)">Cosmopolitan</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Elle_(magazine)" title="Elle (magazine)">Elle</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Grazia" title="Grazia">Grazia</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Men%27s_Health_(magazine)" class="mw-redirect" title="Men's Health (magazine)">Men's Health</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/National_Geographic_(magazine)" title="National Geographic (magazine)">National Geographic</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Le_Monde_diplomatique" title="Le Monde diplomatique">Le Monde diplomatique</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Playboy" title="Playboy">Playboy</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Hello!" class="mw-redirect" title="Hello!">Hello!</a></i> and others.</p>
<p>There are two main news agencies, <a href="/wiki/Beta_News_Agency" title="Beta News Agency">Beta</a> and Fonet.</p>
<p>As of 2014<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Serbia&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the most visited websites in Serbian (mainly on the <a href="/wiki/.rs" title=".rs">.rs</a> domain) are the Serbian version of Google followed by online editions of printed daily <a href="/wiki/Blic" title="Blic">Blic</a>, news web-portal of <a href="/wiki/B92" title="B92">B92</a> broadcaster, news portal of printed daily <a href="/wiki/Kurir" title="Kurir">Kurir</a> and classifieds <a href="/wiki/Kupujemprodajem.com" title="Kupujemprodajem.com">KupujemProdajem</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-297" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-297">[297]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tmulti tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:174px;max-width:174px">
