</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:172px;max-width:172px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Serbian_Christmas_meal.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Serbian_Christmas_meal.jpg/170px-Serbian_Christmas_meal.jpg" width="170" height="128" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Serbian_Christmas_meal.jpg/255px-Serbian_Christmas_meal.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Serbian_Christmas_meal.jpg/340px-Serbian_Christmas_meal.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4581" data-file-height="3448" /></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><a href="/wiki/%C5%A0ljivovica" class="mw-redirect" title="Šljivovica">Šljivovica</a>, Serbian national drink; Serbian <a href="/wiki/Christmas" title="Christmas">Christmas</a> meal</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Serbian_cuisine" title="Serbian cuisine">Serbian cuisine</a></div>
<p>Serbian cuisine is largely heterogeneous, sharing characteristics of the Balkans (especially <a href="/wiki/Former_Yugoslavia" class="mw-redirect" title="Former Yugoslavia">former Yugoslavia</a>), the <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_cuisine" title="Mediterranean cuisine">Mediterranean</a> (<a href="/wiki/Greek_cuisine" title="Greek cuisine">Greek</a> in particular), <a href="/wiki/Turkish_cuisine" title="Turkish cuisine">Turkish</a>, and Central European (especially <a href="/wiki/Austrian_cuisine" title="Austrian cuisine">Austrian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_cuisine" title="Hungarian cuisine">Hungarian</a>) cuisines. Food is very important in Serbian social life, particularly during religious holidays such as <a href="/wiki/Christmas" title="Christmas">Christmas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Easter" title="Easter">Easter</a> and feast days i.e. <a href="/wiki/Slava" title="Slava">slava</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAlbala2011330_298-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAlbala2011330-298">[298]</a></sup></p>
<p>Staples of the Serbian diet include bread, meat, fruits, vegetables, and dairy products. Bread is the basis of all Serbian meals, and it plays an important role in Serbian cuisine and can be found in religious rituals. A traditional Serbian welcome is to offer bread and <a href="/wiki/Salt" title="Salt">salt</a> to guests. Meat is widely consumed, as is fish. Serbian specialties include <a href="/wiki/%C4%86evap%C4%8Di%C4%87i" class="mw-redirect" title="Ćevapčići">ćevapčići</a> (caseless sausages made of minced meat, which is always grilled and seasoned), <a href="/wiki/Pljeskavica" title="Pljeskavica">pljeskavica</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sarma_(food)" title="Sarma (food)">sarma</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kajmak" class="mw-redirect" title="Kajmak">kajmak</a> (a dairy product similar to <a href="/wiki/Clotted_cream" title="Clotted cream">clotted cream</a>), <a href="/wiki/Gibanica" title="Gibanica">gibanica</a> (cheese and kajmak pie), <a href="/wiki/Ajvar" title="Ajvar">ajvar</a> (a roasted red pepper spread), <a href="/wiki/Proja" title="Proja">proja</a> (cornbread), and <a href="/wiki/Ka%C4%8Damak" title="Kačamak">kačamak</a> (corn-flour porridge).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAlbala2011329.E2.80.93330_299-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAlbala2011329.E2.80.93330-299">[299]</a></sup></p>
<p>Serbians claim their country as the birthplace of <a href="/wiki/Rakia" title="Rakia">rakia</a> (<i>rakija</i>), a highly alcoholic drink primarily distilled from fruit. Rakia in various forms is found throughout the Balkans, notably in Bulgaria, Croatia, Slovenia, Montenegro, Hungary and Turkey. <a href="/wiki/Slivovitz" title="Slivovitz">Slivovitz</a> (<i>šljivovica</i>), a plum brandy, is a type of rakia which is considered the national drink of Serbia.<sup id="cite_ref-300" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-300">[300]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_Serbia" title="Sport in Serbia">Sport in Serbia</a></div>
<p>Sports play an important role in Serbian society, and the country has a strong sporting history. The most popular sports in Serbia are <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a>, <a href="/wiki/Basketball" title="Basketball">basketball</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tennis" title="Tennis">tennis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Volleyball" title="Volleyball">volleyball</a>, <a href="/wiki/Water_polo" title="Water polo">water polo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Handball" title="Handball">handball</a>.</p>
<p>Professional sports in Serbia are organized by sporting federations and leagues (in case of team sports). One of particularities of Serbian professional sports is existence of many multi-sports clubs (called "sports societies"), biggest and most successful of which are <a href="/wiki/SD_Crvena_Zvezda" title="SD Crvena Zvezda">Red Star</a>, <a href="/wiki/JSD_Partizan" title="JSD Partizan">Partizan</a>, and <a href="/wiki/OSD_Beograd" title="OSD Beograd">Beograd</a> in Belgrade, <a href="/wiki/SD_Vojvodina" title="SD Vojvodina">Vojvodina</a> in Novi Sad, <a href="/wiki/FK_Radni%C4%8Dki_1923" title="FK Radnički 1923">Radnički</a> in Kragujevac, <a href="/wiki/FK_Spartak_Zlatibor_Voda" class="mw-redirect" title="FK Spartak Zlatibor Voda">Spartak</a> in Subotica.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Paris-FR-75-open_de_tennis-31-5-17-Roland_Garros-Novak_Djokovic-13.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Paris-FR-75-open_de_tennis-31-5-17-Roland_Garros-Novak_Djokovic-13.jpg/220px-Paris-FR-75-open_de_tennis-31-5-17-Roland_Garros-Novak_Djokovic-13.jpg" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Paris-FR-75-open_de_tennis-31-5-17-Roland_Garros-Novak_Djokovic-13.jpg/330px-Paris-FR-75-open_de_tennis-31-5-17-Roland_Garros-Novak_Djokovic-13.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Paris-FR-75-open_de_tennis-31-5-17-Roland_Garros-Novak_Djokovic-13.jpg/440px-Paris-FR-75-open_de_tennis-31-5-17-Roland_Garros-Novak_Djokovic-13.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2477" data-file-height="3303" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Paris-FR-75-open_de_tennis-31-5-17-Roland_Garros-Novak_Djokovic-13.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Novak_Djokovic" title="Novak Djokovic">Novak Djokovic</a>, considered one of the greatest tennis players of all time</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Football is the most popular sport in Serbia, and the <a href="/wiki/Football_Association_of_Serbia" title="Football Association of Serbia">Football Association of Serbia</a> with 146,845 registered players, is the largest sporting association in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-301" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-301">[301]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Dragan_D%C5%BEaji%C4%87" title="Dragan Džajić">Dragan Džajić</a> was officially recognized as "the best Serbian player of all times" by the Football Association of Serbia, and more recently the likes of <a href="/wiki/Nemanja_Vidi%C4%87" title="Nemanja Vidić">Nemanja Vidić</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dejan_Stankovi%C4%87" title="Dejan Stanković">Dejan Stanković</a> and <a href="/wiki/Branislav_Ivanovi%C4%87" title="Branislav Ivanović">Branislav Ivanović</a> play for the elite clubs of Europe, developing the nation's reputation as one of the world's biggest exporters of footballers.<sup id="cite_ref-302" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-302">[302]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Serbia_national_football_team" title="Serbia national football team">Serbia national football team</a> lacks relative success although it qualified for three of the last four <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup" title="FIFA World Cup">FIFA World Cups</a>. Serbia national youth football teams have won <a href="/wiki/2013_UEFA_European_Under-19_Championship" title="2013 UEFA European Under-19 Championship">2013 U-19 European Championship</a> and <a href="/wiki/2015_FIFA_U-20_World_Cup" title="2015 FIFA U-20 World Cup">2015 U-20 World Cup</a>. The two main football clubs in Serbia are <a href="/wiki/Red_Star_Belgrade" title="Red Star Belgrade">Red Star</a> (winner of the <a href="/wiki/1990%E2%80%9391_European_Cup" title="1990–91 European Cup">1991 European Cup</a>) and <a href="/wiki/FK_Partizan" title="FK Partizan">Partizan</a> (finalist of the <a href="/wiki/1965%E2%80%9366_European_Cup" title="1965–66 European Cup">1966 European Cup</a>), both from Belgrade. The rivalry between the two clubs is known as the "<a href="/wiki/Eternal_derby_(Serbia)" class="mw-redirect" title="Eternal derby (Serbia)">Eternal Derby</a>", and is often cited as one of the most exciting sports rivalries in the world.</p>
<p>Serbia is one of the traditional powerhouses of world basketball, as <a href="/wiki/Serbian_national_basketball_team" class="mw-redirect" title="Serbian national basketball team">Serbia men's national basketball team</a> have won two <a href="/wiki/FIBA_World_Championship" class="mw-redirect" title="FIBA World Championship">World Championships</a> (in 1998 and 2002), three <a href="/wiki/EuroBasket" title="EuroBasket">European Championships</a> (1995, 1997, and 2001) and two Olympic silver medals (in <a href="/wiki/Basketball_at_the_1996_Summer_Olympics" title="Basketball at the 1996 Summer Olympics">1996</a> and <a href="/wiki/Basketball_at_the_2016_Summer_Olympics" title="Basketball at the 2016 Summer Olympics">2016</a>) as well. <a href="/wiki/Serbia_women%27s_national_basketball_team" title="Serbia women's national basketball team">The women's national basketball team</a> won the European Championship in 2015 and <a href="/wiki/Basketball_at_the_2016_Summer_Olympics_-_Women%27s_tournament" class="mw-redirect" title="Basketball at the 2016 Summer Olympics - Women's tournament">Olympic bronze medal</a> in 2016. A total of 31 Serbian players have played in the NBA in last two decades, including <a href="/wiki/Peja_Stojakovi%C4%87" title="Peja Stojaković">Predrag "Peja" Stojaković</a> (three-time <a href="/wiki/List_of_NBA_All-Stars" title="List of NBA All-Stars">NBA All-Star</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Vlade_Divac" title="Vlade Divac">Vlade Divac</a> (2001 NBA All-Star and <a href="/wiki/FIBA_Hall_of_Fame" title="FIBA Hall of Fame">FIBA Hall of Famer</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-303" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-303">[303]</a></sup> The renowned "Serbian coaching school" produced many of the most successful European basketball coaches of all times, such as <a href="/wiki/%C5%BDeljko_Obradovi%C4%87" title="Željko Obradović">Željko Obradović</a>, who won a record 9 Euroleague titles as a coach. <a href="/wiki/KK_Partizan" title="KK Partizan">KK Partizan</a> basketball club was the <a href="/wiki/Euroleague_Basketball" title="Euroleague Basketball">1992 European champion</a>.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:RS053-15.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/RS053-15.jpg/220px-RS053-15.jpg" width="220" height="175" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/RS053-15.jpg/330px-RS053-15.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/RS053-15.jpg/440px-RS053-15.jpg 2x" data-file-width="896" data-file-height="712" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:RS053-15.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Serbia_men%27s_national_water_polo_team" title="Serbia men's national water polo team">Serbia men's national water polo team</a> are current Olympic, world and European champions</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Recent success of Serbian tennis players has led to an immense growth in the popularity of tennis in the country. <a href="/wiki/Novak_%C4%90okovi%C4%87" class="mw-redirect" title="Novak Đoković">Novak Đoković</a>, twelve-time <a href="/wiki/Grand_Slam_(tennis)" title="Grand Slam (tennis)">Grand Slam</a> champion, finished in 2011, 2012, 2014 and 2015 as No. 1 in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-304" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-304">[304]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ana_Ivanovic" title="Ana Ivanovic">Ana Ivanovic</a> (champion of <a href="/wiki/2008_French_Open" title="2008 French Open">2008 French Open</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Jelena_Jankovi%C4%87" title="Jelena Janković">Jelena Janković</a> were both ranked No. 1 in the WTA Rankings. There were two No. 1 ranked-tennis double players as well: <a href="/wiki/Nenad_Zimonji%C4%87" title="Nenad Zimonjić">Nenad Zimonjić</a> (three-time men's double and four-time mixed double Grand Slam champion) and <a href="/wiki/Slobodan_%C5%BDivojinovi%C4%87" title="Slobodan Živojinović">Slobodan Živojinović</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Serbia_Davis_Cup_team" title="Serbia Davis Cup team">Serbia men's tennis national team</a> won the <a href="/wiki/2010_Davis_Cup" title="2010 Davis Cup">2010 Davis Cup</a> while <a href="/wiki/Serbia_Fed_Cup_team" title="Serbia Fed Cup team">Serbia women's tennis national team</a> reached the final at <a href="/wiki/2012_Fed_Cup" title="2012 Fed Cup">2012 Fed Cup</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-305" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-305">[305]</a></sup></p>
<p>Serbia is one of the leading volleyball countries in the world. Its <a href="/wiki/Serbia_men%27s_national_volleyball_team" title="Serbia men's national volleyball team">men's national team</a> won the <a href="/wiki/Volleyball_at_the_2000_Summer_Olympics" title="Volleyball at the 2000 Summer Olympics">gold medal at 2000 Olympics</a>, and has won the <a href="/wiki/Men%27s_European_Volleyball_Championship" title="Men's European Volleyball Championship">European Championship</a> twice. The <a href="/wiki/Serbia_women%27s_national_volleyball_team" title="Serbia women's national volleyball team">women's national volleyball team</a> won the <a href="/wiki/Women%27s_European_Volleyball_Championship" title="Women's European Volleyball Championship">European Championship</a> twice as well as <a href="/wiki/Volleyball_at_the_2016_Summer_Olympics_-_Women%27s_tournament" class="mw-redirect" title="Volleyball at the 2016 Summer Olympics - Women's tournament">Olympic silver medal</a> in 2016.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Serbia_men%27s_national_water_polo_team" title="Serbia men's national water polo team">Serbia men's national water polo team</a> is the second most successful national team after Hungary, having won Olympic gold medal in 2016, three <a href="/wiki/Water_polo_at_the_World_Aquatics_Championships" title="Water polo at the World Aquatics Championships">World Championships</a> (2005, 2009 and 2015), and six <a href="/wiki/European_Water_Polo_Championship" title="European Water Polo Championship">European Championships</a> in 2001, 2003, 2006, 2012, 2014 and 2016 respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-306" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-306">[306]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/VK_Partizan" title="VK Partizan">VK Partizan</a> has won a joint-record seven <a href="/wiki/LEN_Euroleague" class="mw-redirect" title="LEN Euroleague">European champion</a> titles.</p>
<p>Other noted Serbian athletes include: swimmers <a href="/wiki/Milorad_%C4%8Cavi%C4%87" title="Milorad Čavić">Milorad Čavić</a> (2009 World champion on 50 meters butterfly and silver medalist on 100 meters butterfly as well as 2008 Olympic silver medalist on 100 meters butterfly in <a href="/wiki/Swimming_at_the_2008_Summer_Olympics_%E2%80%93_Men%27s_100_metre_butterfly" title="Swimming at the 2008 Summer Olympics – Men's 100 metre butterfly">historic race with American swimmer Michael Phelps</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Na%C4%91a_Higl" title="Nađa Higl">Nađa Higl</a> (2009 World champion in 200 meters breaststroke – the first Serbian woman to become a world champion in swimming); track and field athlete <a href="/wiki/Ivana_%C5%A0panovi%C4%87" title="Ivana Španović">Ivana Španović</a> (long-jumper; 2016 European champion and bronze medalist at the <a href="/wiki/2016_Olympics" class="mw-redirect" title="2016 Olympics">2016 Olympics</a>); wrestler <a href="/wiki/Davor_%C5%A0tefanek" title="Davor Štefanek">Davor Štefanek</a> (2016 Olympic gold medalist), and taekwondoist <a href="/wiki/Milica_Mandi%C4%87" title="Milica Mandić">Milica Mandić</a> (2012 Olympic gold medalist).</p>
<p>Serbia has hosted several major sport competitions in the last ten years, including the <a href="/wiki/2005_EuroBasket" class="mw-redirect" title="2005 EuroBasket">2005 Men's European Basketball Championship</a>, <a href="/wiki/2005_Men%27s_European_Volleyball_Championship" title="2005 Men's European Volleyball Championship">2005 Men's European Volleyball Championship</a>, 2006 and 2016 Men's European Water Polo Championships, <a href="/wiki/2009_Summer_Universiade" title="2009 Summer Universiade">2009 Summer Universiade</a>, <a href="/wiki/2012_European_Men%27s_Handball_Championship" title="2012 European Men's Handball Championship">2012 European Men's Handball Championship</a>, and <a href="/wiki/2013_World_Women%27s_Handball_Championship" title="2013 World Women's Handball Championship">2013 World Women's Handball Championship</a>. The most important annual sporting events held in the country are <a href="/wiki/Belgrade_Marathon" title="Belgrade Marathon">Belgrade Marathon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tour_de_Serbie" title="Tour de Serbie">Tour de Serbie</a> cycling race.</p>
